so here is ashdown's third law .	這就是第三個法律 。
by the way , don't ask me about ashdown's first law and second law because i haven't invented those yet ; it always sounds better if there's a third law , doesn't it ?	順便一提 , 別問我 , 第二個法律和第二個法律 , 因為我沒有發明過這些 ; 它總是聽起來更好 , 如果有第三個法律 , 不是嗎 ?
ashdown's third law is that in the modern age , where everything is connected to everything , the most important thing about what you can do is what you can do with others .	第三個法則是 , 在現代時代 , 一切都連結到所有東西都連結到所有東西 , 最重要的是你能做什麼的 。
the most important bit about your structure whether you're a government , whether you're an army regiment , whether you're a business is your docking points , your interconnectors , your capacity to network with others .	最重要的是 , 你的結構是否是個政府 , 不論你是個軍隊 , 不論你是個企業的點子 , 你的內心和其他人之間的能力 。
you understand that in industry ; governments don't .	你了解工業 ; 政府不用 。
but now one final thing .	但現在有一個最後一件最後的事 。
if it is the case , ladies and gentlemen and it is that we are now locked together in a way that has never been quite the same before , then it's also the case that we share a destiny with each other .	如果這是這樣 , 女士們 , 女士們 , 我們現在被鎖定在某種程度上 , 那也是我們從未曾和彼此分享的案例 。
suddenly and for the very first time , collective defense , the thing that has dominated us as the concept of securing our nations , is no longer enough .	突然間 , 收集破壞了 , 收集我們的國家 , 收集我們國家的概念 , 不是足夠的 。
it used to be the case that if my tribe was more powerful than their tribe , i was safe ; if my country was more powerful than their country , i was safe ; my alliance , like nato , was more powerful than their alliance , i was safe .	以前 , 如果我的部落比他們的部落更強大 , 我國家安全 ; 如果我的國家比他們的國家更強強大 , 我都安全 ; 我都安全 。
it is no longer the case .	它不再是案例 。
the advent of the interconnectedness and of the weapons of mass destruction means that , increasingly , i share a destiny with my enemy .	聯合國際武器和武器的武器 , 很快地 , 我和敵人的武器 。
when i was a diplomat negotiating the disarmament treaties with the soviet union in geneva in the 1970s , we succeeded because we understood we shared a destiny with them .	當我在1970年代時 , 我和蘇聯聯的遺傳治療 , 在1970年代 , 我們成功地了解到 , 因為我們了解到 , 我們共享了一場辯論 。
collective security is not enough .	集體安全並不夠 。
peace has come to northern ireland because both sides realized that the zerosum game couldn't work .	平靜必須北極 , 因為兩邊都知道 , 零和遊戲無法運作 。

and so suddenly , ladies and gentlemen , what has been the proposition of visionaries and poets down the ages becomes something we have to take seriously as a matter of public policy .	所以突然間 , 女士們們 , 女士們們 , 那些年齡和資產 , 年齡就變成我們必須認真地認真地作為公共政政策的重要性 。
i started with a poem , i'll end with one .	我從一首詩開始 , 我會跟一個詩歌 。

for us , i think , part of the equation for our survival .	對我們來說 , 我認為 , 是我們生存的一部分 。
to find the path to long life and health , dan buettner and team study the world's " blue zones , " communities whose elders live with vim and vigor to recordsetting age . at tedxtc , he shares the 9 common diet and lifestyle habits that keep them spry past age 100 .	為了尋找長壽生命和健康、丹佛佛和團隊一起研究世界的 「 藍zone 」 的社區 」 、 「 藍zones 」 的社區 , 他分享了9個共同飲食和生活方式 , 他分享了9個共同飲食和生活方式 。
biology , culture , exploration , food , health , life , science	生物學、文化、探索、食物、健康、健康、生命、科學、科學、生命、科學、
dan buettner: how to live to be 100+	丹佛佛佛佛佛佛:要如何活到100個+ 。
something called the danish twin study established that only about 10 percent of how long the average person lives , within certain biological limits , is dictated by our genes .	叫做丹佛研究建議 , 只有百分之十的平均壽命 , 在某些生物限制中 , 在某些生物限制中 , 被我們的基因限制 。
the other 90 percent is dictated by our lifestyle .	另外90%的壽命是死亡的 。
so the premise of blue zones: if we can find the optimal lifestyle of longevity we can come up with a de facto formula for longevity .	所以藍zone的預防:如果我們可以找到最佳的生活方式 , 我們就能找到最佳的生命方式 。
but if you ask the average american what the optimal formula of longevity is , they probably couldn't tell you .	但如果你問一個平均美國最樂觀的平均壽命是 , 他們可能無法告訴你 。
they've probably heard of the south beach diet , or the atkins diet .	他們可能聽過南海灘飲食 , 或是皮膚飲食 。

the fact of the matter is there is a lot of confusion around what really helps us live longer better .	重要的是 , 有許多困惑的事實是 , 幫助我們活得更好 。
should you be running marathons or doing yoga ?	你應該要跑馬拉松或做瑜伽 ?
should you eat organic meats or should you be eating tofu ?	你應該要吃有機機肉或你應該吃東西嗎 ?
when it comes to supplements , should you be taking them ?	當它到供應時 , 你應該要把它們放到嗎 ?
how about these hormones or resveratrol ?	這些荷爾蒙或回收者呢 ?
and does purpose play into it ?	目的是嗎 ?
spirituality ? and how about how we socialize ?	精神嗎 ? 我們要如何社會化 ?
well , our approach to finding longevity was to team up with national geographic , and the national institute on aging , to find the four demographically confirmed areas that are geographically defined .	嗯 , 我們的方法找到長期的長期是要與國家地理合作 , 找到四度的國家組織 , 找到四度的區域 , 找到四度的四度 。
and then bring a team of experts in there to methodically go through exactly what these people do , to distill down the crosscultural distillation .	然後帶了一群專家團隊的專家團隊 , 將這些人分散到這些人所做的 , 把文化分割成 。
and at the end of this i'm going to tell you what that distillation is .	最後我要告訴各位 , 我要告訴各位什麼樣的 。
but first i'd like to debunk some common myths when it comes to longevity .	但首先 , 我想要辯論一些常見的謎題 。
and the first myth is if you try really hard you can live to be 100 .	第一個謎題是如果你真的很難活到100歲 。
the problem is , only about one out of 5 , 000 people in america live to be 100 .	問題是 , 只有大約五千萬人住在美國 。
your chances are very low .	你的機會非常低 。
even though it's the fastest growing demographic in america , it's hard to reach 100 .	即使是美國最快成長的人口 , 很難達到100倍 。
the problem is that we're not programmed for longevity .	問題是 , 我們不是很長久的 。
we are programmed for something called procreative success .	我們被程式設計成了一個叫做 「 成功 」 。
i love that word .	我喜歡這個詞 。
it reminds me of my college days .	它提醒我大學的大學 。
biologists term procreative success to mean the age where you have children and then another generation , the age when your children have children .	生物學家的進步是指指指指出你有孩子和另一代世代 , 另一代 , 當你的孩子有孩子 。
after that the effect of evolution completely dissipates .	在進化過程中 , 完全分散了 。
if you're a mammal , if you're a rat or an elephant , or a human , in between , it's the same story .	如果你是個哺乳動物 , 若你是一隻兔子或大象 , 或人類之間之間 , 它是同樣的故事 。
so to make it to age 100 , you not only have to have had a very good lifestyle , you also have to have won the genetic lottery .	所以為了讓它達成100歲 , 你不僅需要有很好的生命方式 , 你也必須贏得基因 。
the second myth is , there are treatments that can help slow , reverse , or even stop aging .	第二個謎題是 , 有治療方法可以慢、逆轉、回報、甚至停止協調 。
when you think of it , there is 99 things that can age us .	當你想到它時 , 有999個東西可以讓我們的年齡 。
deprive your brain of oxygen for just a few minutes , those brain cells die , they never come back .	描述你的氧氣的大腦 , 幾分鐘 , 那些腦細胞死去 , 他們從來沒有回來 。
play tennis too hard , on your knees , ruin your cartilage , the cartilage never comes back .	玩家太困難了 , 在你的膝蓋上 , 車子從來沒有回來 。
our arteries can clog . our brains can gunk up with plaque , and we can get alzheimer's .	我們的藝術家可以哭泣
there is just too many things to go wrong .	有太多東西去錯了 。
our bodies have 35 trillion cells , trillion with a " t . " we're talking national debt numbers here .	我們的身體有35兆個細胞 , 試想一下 「 t 。 」 我們現在正在談論國家辯論數字 。
those cells turn themselves over once every eight years .	這些細胞將自己轉換到每八年 。
and every time they turn themselves over there is some damage . and that damage builds up .	每當他們把自己轉移到那裡有一些損傷
and it builds up exponentially .	基本上它建造出出昂貴的 。
it's a little bit like the days when we all had beatles albums or eagles albums and we'd make a copy of that on a cassette tape , and let our friends copy that cassette tape , and pretty soon , with successive generations that tape sounds like garbage .	這有點像我們一樣都有脂肪脂肪酸或蛋白質的日子 , 我們會製造一套貓咪的複製品 , 讓我們的朋友的複製品 , 讓我們的朋友們一起合作 , 很快地 , 和成功的代價 , 和成功的成果 。
well , the same things happen to our cells .	嗯 , 同樣的事情發生在我們的細胞身上 。
that's why a 65yearold person is aging at a rate of about 125 times faster than a 12yearold person .	這就是為什麼一名65歲的年輕人在同意大約125倍 。
so , if there is nothing you can do to slow your aging or stop your aging , what am i doing here ?	所以 , 如果沒有辦法把你的狗放慢或停止你的狗 , 我在這裡做些什麼 ?
well , the fact of the matter is the best science tells us that the capacity of the human body , my body , your body , is about 90 years , a little bit more for women .	重要的是 , 最重要的科學告訴我們人類身體的能力 , 我的身體 , 你的身體 , 你的身體 , 大約90年 , 有點像女性一樣 。
but life expectancy in this country is only 78 .	但這國家的壽命只有78歲 。
so somewhere along the line , we're leaving about 12 good years on the table .	所以有些地方 , 我們在桌上留下大約12年 。
these are years that we could get .	這些是我們能得到的 。
and research shows that they would be years largely free of chronic disease , heart disease , cancer and diabetes .	研究顯示 , 牠們會很大的免費疾病、心臟疾病、糖尿病、糖尿病、糖尿病、糖尿病 。
we think the best way to get these missing years is to look at the cultures around the world that are actually experiencing them , areas where people are living to age 100 at rates up to 10 times greater than we are , areas where the life expectancy is an extra dozen years , the rate of middle age mortality is a fraction of what it is in this country .	我們認為最好的方法是去觀察世界各地的文化 , 實際上人們生活在擴大到10倍 , 人們生活在哪裡 , 比我們所居住的百倍 , 比我們所期待的百倍 。
we found our first blue zone about 125 miles off the coast of italy , on the island of sardinia .	我們發現我們的第一個藍色zone大約125英哩的海岸區域 。
and not the entire island , the island is about 1 . 4 million people , but only up in the highlands , an area called the nuoro province .	而不是整個島嶼 , 島嶼大約有1.4百萬人 , 但只有在高島上 , 一個叫做 「 營利 」 。
and here we have this area where men live the longest , about 10 times more centenarians than we have here in america .	這裡我們有這位區域男人活著最長的10倍 , 比我們在美國所擁有的10倍 。
and this is a place where people not only reach age 100 , they do so with extraordinary vigor .	這是人們不只是達到100歲的村莊 , 他們和極端的村莊 。
places where 102 year olds still ride their bike to work , chop wood , and can beat a guy 60 years younger than them .	在102歲時仍然把他們的腳踏上工作、chopwod , 可以成為一個人六十歲的年輕人 。
their history actually goes back to about the time of christ .	他們的歷史其實回到聖誕時代 。
it's actually a bronze age culture that's been isolated .	其實是一輛布朗克羅斯的文化 。
because the land is so infertile , they largely are shepherds , which occasions regular , lowintensity physical activity .	因為土地是非常感染的 , 它們大部份是羊毛、低溫的物理活動 。
their diet is mostly plantbased , accentuated with foods that they can carry into the fields .	他們的飲食是大部分植物都能把它們帶到田園裡 。
they came up with an unleavened whole wheat bread called carta musica made out of durum wheat , a type of cheese made from grassfed animals so the cheese is high in omega3 fatty acids instead of omega6 fatty acids from cornfed animals , and a type of wine that has three times the level of polyphenols than any known wine in the world .	他們從一個未被忽略了 , 叫做卡塔音樂aata音樂製作出來的曲子 , 一類廚房是由灰色的動物所組成的高度 , 而不是來自珊瑚礁的動物 , 而是從珊瑚礁中獲取的三倍 。
but the real secret i think lies more in the way that they organize their society .	但真正秘密我認為謊言的方式是他們組織的社會 。
and one of the most salient elements of the sardinian society is how they treat older people .	而其中一個最恐怖的元素之一就是他們如何治療更老的人 。
you ever notice here in america , social equity seems to peak at about age 24 ?	你沒有注意到美國、社會平等似乎在24歲的時候 ?
just look at the advertisements .	看看廣告 。
here in sardinia , the older you get the more equity you have , the more wisdom you're celebrated for .	在ardinia , 越長你有越平等你有越多的智慧 。
you go into the bars in sardinia , instead of seeing the sports illustrated swimsuit calendar , you see the centenarian of the month calendar .	你進入芝加哥州的酒店 , 而不是看到運動場的運動 , 而是月球的月球 。
this , as it turns out , is not only good for your aging parents to keep them close to the family it imparts about four to six years of extra life expectancy research shows it's also good for the children of those families , who have lower rates of mortality and lower rates of disease .	結果發現 , 不僅對你的父母來說 , 不只對你的家人來說 , 大約四到六年間的家庭研究顯示 , 這也是對那些家庭的孩童壽命和低率較低 。
that's called the grandmother effect .	叫做祖母效應效應 。
we found our second blue zone on the other side of the planet , about 800 miles south of tokyo , on the archipelago of okinawa .	我們發現我們的第二個藍色zone在地球上 , 大約800英里南方的南方方 。
okinawa is actually 161 small islands .	okinawa是161小島嶼 。
and in the northern part of the main island , this is ground zero for world longevity .	在主要島嶼的北極地區 , 這是地球長期的零件 。
this is a place where the oldest living female population is found .	這是一個最古老的活生生生生生存的地方 。
it's a place where people have the longest disabilityfree life expectancy in the world .	這是世界上人們有最長的殘疾壽命的地方 。
they have what we want .	他們有我們想要的 。
they live a long time , and tend to die in their sleep , very quickly , and often , i can tell you , after sex .	他們活得很長的時間 , 通常會死在睡眠中 , 通常 , 我可以告訴你 , 在性別上 。
they live about seven good years longer than the average american .	他們住在美國平均壽命超過七年 。
five times as many centenarians as we have in america .	我們在美國有五倍的五倍 。
one fifth the rate of colon and breast cancer , big killers here in america .	一分五分之二的蟻群率和乳癌 , 大殺害者在這裡 。
and one sixth the rate of cardiovascular disease .	一分六分之一的汽車疾病率 。
and the fact that this culture has yielded these numbers suggests strongly they have something to teach us .	事實上 , 這個文化已經被告知了這些數字 , 他們必須教導我們 。
what do they do ?	他們怎麼做 ?
once again , a plantbased diet , full of vegetables with lots of color in them .	再一次 , 一個植物飲食 , 充滿蔬菜 , 充滿了許多顏色 。
and they eat about eight times as much tofu as americans do .	他們吃了大約八倍的美國人 。
more significant than what they eat is how they eat it .	比他們吃什麼 , 比他們吃什麼 ?
they have all kinds of little strategies to keep from overeating , which , as you know , is a big problem here in america .	他們有各種策略 , 讓美國脫離的策略 , 如你所知 , 這是美國最大的問題 。
a few of the strategies we observed: they eat off of smaller plates , so they tend to eat fewer calories at every sitting .	我們觀察了一些策略:他們吃掉更多的策略 , 所以他們會吃更多的計算 , 所以他們通常會吃更多的計算機 。
instead of serving family style , where you can sort of mindlessly eat as you're talking , they serve at the counter , put the food away , and then bring it to the table .	不是提供家庭壓力 , 不管你說話 , 你可以把食物當作你說話 , 他們在郡旁邊 , 然後把食物放到桌上 , 然後把它帶到桌上 。
they also have a 3 , 000yearold adage , which i think is the greatest sort of diet suggestion ever invented .	他們也有三千歲的阿姨 , 我認為這是史上最偉大的飲食 。
it was invented by confucius .	它是由難民發明的 。
and that diet is known as the hara , hatchi , bu diet .	這飲食是 「 哈拉、哈拉、哈頓、哈頓、虐待 。
it's simply a little saying these people say before their meal to remind them to stop eating when their stomach is [80] percent full .	這只是個小說 , 這些人說在他們的胃裡 , 讓他們停止吃掉時 , 80%完整 。
it takes about a half hour for that full feeling to travel from your belly to your brain .	它需要大約一半小時的感覺 , 從你的蜜蜂到你的腦袋裡 。
and by remembering to stop at 80 percent it helps keep you from doing that very thing .	記住 , 記住80% , 幫助你保持這樣做 。
but , like sardinia , okinawa has a few social constructs that we can associate with longevity .	但 , 就像ardinia , okinawa有幾個社交建設 , 我們可以與長久久的社會建設 。
we know that isolation kills .	我們知道 , 被殺害 。
fifteen years ago , the average american had three good friends .	五十年前 , 平均美國有三個好朋友 。
we're down to one and half right now .	我們現在下降到一半 。
if you were lucky enough to be born in okinawa , you were born into a system where you automatically have a half a dozen friends with whom you travel through life .	如果你很幸運的是 , 你出生於加州的一個系統 , 你出生了一半的朋友 , 你就自動了一半的朋友 。
they call it a moai . and if you're in a moai you're expected to share the bounty if you encounter luck , and if things go bad , child gets sick , parent dies , you always have somebody who has your back .	他們稱它為 「 莫札特 , 如果你在一個月球上你預期幸運 , 如果你遇到幸運 , 如果你遇到壞事 , 你總是有你的背景 , 你總是有你的背景 。
this particular moai , these five ladies have been together for 97 years .	這五個女士 , 這五個女士都聚在一起了 。
their average age is 102 .	他們的平均是102歲 。
typically in america we've divided our adult life up into two sections .	通常在美國 , 我們已經被分成了兩種選擇 。
there is our work life , where we're productive .	有我們的工作 , 我們的工作是生產力的 。
and then one day , boom , we retire .	然後有一天 , 我們退休了 。
and typically that has meant retiring to the easy chair , or going down to arizona to play golf .	通常這意味著重新思考簡單椅子的椅子 , 或者下到監獄 。
in the okinawan language there is not even a word for retirement .	在加州的語言中 , 甚至沒有對抗抗抗拒 。
instead there is one word that imbues your entire life , and that word is " ikigai . "	反而不是有一種詞彙 , 那就是 「 我kigai 」
and , roughly translated , it means " the reason for which you wake up in the morning . "	而且 , 早上翻譯 , 意思是: 「 你在早上醒來 。 」
for this 102yearold karate master , his ikigai was carrying forth this martial art .	大約102歲的karatemater , 他的ikigai正在追蹤這個火星藝術 。
for this hundredyearold fisherman it was continuing to catch fish for his family three times a week .	對這百歲的漁夫人來說 , 一直在持續捕撈漁夫的三倍 。
and this is a question . the national institute on aging actually gave us a questionnaire to give these centenarians .	這是個問題
and one of the questions , they were very culturally astute , the people who put the questionnaire .	而其中一個問題之一 , 他們非常靈魂的鮪魚之一 。
one of the questions was , " what is your ikigai ? "	其中一個問題是: 「 你的ikigai ? 」
they instantly knew why they woke up in the morning .	他們很明顯地知道為什麼他們在早上醒來 。
for this 102 year old woman , her ikigai was simply her greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	大約102歲的女人 , 她的ikigai只是她偉大的宗教 。
two girls separated in age by 101 and a half years .	兩位女孩分開在10150年半 。
and i asked her what it felt like to hold a greatgreatgreatgranddaughter .	然後我問她什麼感覺 , 把一個偉大的宗教認知 。
and she put her head back and she said , " it feels like leaping into heaven . "	她把她放在頭上 , 她說: 「 這感覺就像在天堂上 。 」
i thought that was a wonderful thought .	我想那是個很棒的思想 。
my editor at geographic wanted me to find america's blue zone .	我的編輯者希望我找到美國是藍色的 。
and for a while we looked on the prairies of minnesota , where actually there is a very high proportion of centenarians .	儘管我們看著骨頭的鏡頭 , 實際上有一個非常高的進展 。
but that's because all the young people left .	但這是因為所有年輕人離開了 。
so , we turned to the data again .	所以 , 我們再轉到資料 。
and we found america's longestlived population among the seventhday adventists concentrated in and around loma linda , california .	我們發現美國最長期的人口是七天的人口 , 在倫敦 , 加州 , 加州 , 加州 , 加州 。
adventists are conservative methodists .	保守者是保守主義者 。
they celebrate their sabbath from sunset on friday till sunset on saturday .	他們慶祝他們的日常生活在星期六的日日常生活中 。
a " 24hour sanctuary in time , " they call it .	一旦24小時的聖誕節 , 他們稱它為它 。
and they follow five little habits that conveys to them extraordinary longevity , comparatively speaking .	他們遵循五個小棲息地的棲息地 , 相反地說話 。
in america here , life expectancy for the average woman is 80 .	在美國 , 生活期望女性的期望是80歲 。
but for an adventist woman , their life expectancy is 89 .	但對一位一位一位女士 , 他們的壽命是89年 。
and the difference is even more pronounced among men , who are expected to live about 11 years longer than their american counterparts .	差別的差異比比他們的美國人多 , 他們預期壽命超過11年 。
now , this is a study that followed about 70 , 000 people for 30 years .	這是一項研究 , 追蹤了大約七萬人 。
sterling study . and i think it supremely illustrates the premise of this blue zone project .	史蒂芬研究了 , 我認為它對藍色zone計畫的總統計計畫 。
this is a heterogeneous community .	這是個很棒的社區 。
it's white , black , hispanic , asian .	這是白人、黑人、他的panic ,
the only thing that they have in common are a set of very small lifestyle habits that they follow ritualistically for most of their lives .	他們唯一共同的共同生活方式就是他們遵循非常小的習慣 。
they take their diet directly from the bible .	他們把他們的飲食直接從麵包中拿出來 。
genesis: chapter one , verse [29] , where god talks about legumes and seeds , and on one more stanza about green plants , ostensibly missing is meat .	基因is:查爾斯.1、29年 , 上帝談論法律 , 上帝還有更多關於綠色植物、十二氧化植物、十二氧化植物、十二氧化碳 。
they take this sanctuary in time very serious .	他們在時間非常嚴肅 。
for 24 hours every week , no matter how busy they are , how stressed out they are at work , where the kids need to be driven , they stop everything and they focus on their god , their social network , and then , hardwired right in the religion , are nature walks .	每週每週每週 , 都不管他們在工作時 , 不管他們在工作 , 孩子需要被驅動 , 他們停止所有東西都在他們的社會網絡上 , 然後很難在宗教、自然網路上、自然的走路 。
and the power of this is not that it's done occasionally , the power is it's done every week for a lifetime .	這並不是這樣做 , 而是每週的力量 , 權力是每週完成的 。
none of it's hard . none of it costs money .	沒有錢 , 沒有它成本錢 。
adventists also tend to hang out with other adventists .	愛滋病學家也傾向於其他進步 。
so , if you go to an adventist's party you don't see people swilling jim beam or rolling a joint .	所以 , 如果你去參加一位舞者的夥伴 , 你看不到人們游泳jim蜜蜂或滾樂團 。
instead they're talking about their next nature walk , exchanging recipes , and yes , they pray .	反而他們正在談論他們的下一步 , 他們祈禱 。 是的 , 他們祈禱 。
but they influence each other in profound and measurable ways .	但他們影響彼此的影響 。
this is a culture that has yielded ellsworth whareham .	這是一種文化 , 被告知埃及的文化 。
ellsworth whareham is 97 years old .	ellhamhamreham是97歲的 。
he's a multimillionaire , yet when a contractor wanted 6 , 000 dollars to build a privacy fence , he said , " for that kind of money i'll do it myself . "	他是多數的多樣性 , 但當一個矛盾想要6 , 000美金來建造一個隱私的法律 , 他說: 「 錢我會這麼做 。 」
so for the next three days he was out shoveling cement , and hauling poles around .	所以接下來的三天 , 他被震驚了 , 把粒子放在周圍 。
and predictably , perhaps , on the fourth day he ended up in the operating room .	預測一下 , 也許 , 第四天 , 他終於在手術室裡 。
but not as the guy on the table ; the guy doing openheart surgery .	但不是當桌子上的傢伙 , 那個人在做開放手術 。

and the first one , and i'm about to utter a heresy here , none of them exercise , at least the way we think of exercise .	首先 , 我要在這裡要在這裡 , 沒有人特別興奮 , 至少我們認為練習 。
instead , they set up their lives so that they are constantly nudged into physical activity .	相反地 , 他們設立了他們的生命活動 , 所以他們通常被分成身體活動 。
these 100yearold okinawan women are getting up and down off the ground , they sit on the floor , 30 or 40 times a day .	這些100歲的女兒在地板上 , 他們坐在地面上 , 坐下來 , 他們坐在地板上 , 30到40倍 。
sardinians live in vertical houses , up and down the stairs .	ardinian住在垂直房子裡 , 然後下樓梯 。
every trip to the store , or to church or to a friend's house occasions a walk .	每次嘗試到店裡 , 或者教堂或朋友的房子 。
they don't have any conveniences .	他們沒有任何關心 。

that burns calories just as much as going on the treadmill does .	那燃燒的卡路里 , 燃燒的卡路里 。
when they do do intentional physical activity , it's the things they enjoy . they tend to walk , the only proven way to stave off cognitive decline , and they all tend to have a garden .	當他們做獨立的物理活動時 , 這是他們享受認知的事物 , 他們會傾向走路 , 唯一能進展 , 他們都傾向於一個花園 , 他們都傾向於花園 。
they know how to set up their life in the right way so they have the right outlook .	他們知道如何在右邊設定他們的生命 。
each of these cultures take time to downshift .	每一個文化都需要時間轉變 。

but when you're in a hurry or stressed out , that triggers something called the inflammatory response , which is associated with everything from alzheimer's disease to cardiovascular disease .	但當你在一個颶風或壓力時 , 蛋白質反應器時 , 蛋白質反應爐中 , 也就是從阿茲海默疾病到卡洛斯疾病的所有東西都來自阿茲海默疾病 。
when you slow down for 15 minutes a day you turn that inflammatory state into a more antiinflammatory state .	當你慢下降了15分鐘 , 你會轉變成更抗體狀態狀態的狀態 。

doesn't mean they don't eat meat , but lots of beans and nuts .	不表示他們不吃肉 , 但很多蜜蜂和營養 。
and they have strategies to keep from overeating , little things that nudge them away from the table at the right time .	他們有策略來保持策略 , 從右邊開始 , 把他們從桌子移到桌子上 。
and then the foundation of all this is how they connect .	接著 , 所有這些都是他們連結的 。
they put their families first , take care of their children and their aging parents .	他們把他們的家庭首先 , 照顧他們的孩子和他們的父母 。
they all tend to belong to a faithbased community , which is worth between four and 14 extra years of life expectancy if you do it four times a month .	他們都傾向於一個信仰社群的社區 , 這是值四分之四的壽命 , 如果你有1月4倍的壽命 。
and the biggest thing here is they also belong to the right tribe .	這裡最棒的是 , 他們也屬於正確的部落 。
they were either born into or they proactively surrounded themselves with the right people .	他們生於出生 , 或是他們對對對權的人感到驕傲 。
we know from the framingham studies , that if your three best friends are obese there is a 50 percent better chance that you'll be overweight .	我們從碎片開始知道如果三個最好的朋友是肥胖的 。
so , if you hang out with unhealthy people , that's going to have a measurable impact over time .	所以 , 如果你和沒有財富的人 , 那將會有很大的影響 。
instead , if your friend's idea of recreation is physical activity , bowling , or playing hockey , biking or gardening , if your friends drink a little , but not too much , and they eat right , and they're engaged , and they're trusting and trustworthy , that is going to have the biggest impact over time .	相反的是 , 如果你的朋友的想法是物理活動的 , 或是在玩笑 , 或花園或花園 , 如果你的朋友喝酒 , 但不太太太太多了 , 他們會吃錯 , 但他們很有信任、信任、信任、信任、信任、信任、信任、信任、信任 。
diets don't work . no diet in the history of the world has ever worked for more than two percent of the population .	恐龍不行 , 世界上沒有死於2%的人口歷史歷史 。
exercise programs usually start in january ; they're usually done by october .	很明顯的程式通常從日本開始 , 他們通常是由十月月球所做的 。
when it comes to longevity there is no short term fix in a pill or anything else .	當它到長期的長期 , 沒有短期的纖維或其他東西 。
but when you think about it , your friends are longterm adventures , and therefore , perhaps the most significant thing you can do to add more years to your life , and life to your years . thank you very much .	但當你想到它時 , 你的朋友很長期 , 你的朋友很久 , 也許你能做更多的事 , 或許你能做到更多年的時間 , 謝謝大家 。
ink that conducts electricity ; a window that turns from clear to opaque at the flip of a switch ; a jelly that makes music . all this stuff exists , and catarina mota says: it's time to play with it . mota leads us on a tour of surprising and cool new materials , and suggests that the way we'll figure out what they're good for is to experiment , tinker and have fun .	在那之後 , 產生電力的窗戶 ; 窗戶的窗戶中 , 從清晰到opa的飛行器 ; 一個珠寶可以用它來玩音樂 。 克里娜•莫特說:那時候要讓我們驚訝的是 , 要讓我們驚訝的是 , 為了讓我們感到驚訝 。
creativity , design , technology	創造力、設計、科技、科技 。
catarina mota: play with smart materials	catarinamota:用智慧材料來玩 。
i have a friend in portugal whose grandfather built a vehicle out of a bicycle and a washing machine so he could transport his family .	我有一個朋友在葡萄牙建造了一座飛行器建造了一台飛機 , 一台機器可以運送他的家人 。
he did it because he couldn't afford a car , but also because he knew how to build one .	他這麼做是因為他無法負擔汽車 , 但也是因為他知道如何建立一個車子 。
there was a time when we understood how things worked and how they were made , so we could build and repair them , or at the very least make informed decisions about what to buy .	當我們了解到如何運作時 , 我們就能建立和修復它們如何運作、修復它們 , 或至少至少在買什麼 。
many of these doityourself practices were lost in the second half of the 20th century .	在20世紀以來 , 很多人都失去在20世紀的第二半 。
but now , the maker community and the opensource model are bringing this kind of knowledge about how things work and what they're made of back into our lives , and i believe we need to take them to the next level , to the components things are made of .	但現在 , 製造家社區和開放的知識模式將這類知識帶回我們的生命中 , 我相信我們需要把它們帶回下一層層層樓 , 我相信我們要把它們帶到下一個層 。
for the most part , we still know what traditional materials like paper and textiles are made of and how they are produced .	最重要的部分 , 我們仍然知道傳統材料是什麼樣子 , 文字、文字、文字、文字、如何產生 。
but now we have these amazing , futuristic composites plastics that change shape , paints that conduct electricity , pigments that change color , fabrics that light up .	但現在我們有這些驚人、自閉症的塑膠塑膠、顏色、顏色、顏色、顏色、顏色、顏色的顏色 。
let me show you some examples .	讓我舉個例子 。
so conductive ink allows us to paint circuits instead of using the traditional printed circuit boards or wires .	所以 , 藉由讓我們痛苦的情境 , 而不是用傳統印刷電路板印刷板或推特 。
in the case of this little example i'm holding , we used it to create a touch sensor that reacts to my skin by turning on this little light .	在這個小例子中 , 我們用它來製造一種感應器來觸碰我的皮膚 。
conductive ink has been used by artists , but recent developments indicate that we will soon be able to use it in laser printers and pens .	根據藝術家所用的藝術家 , 但最近最近發展出的發展 , 很快就會使用它 , 在雷射印刷機和鉛筆 。
and this is a sheet of acrylic infused with colorless lightdiffusing particles .	這是個令人難以置信的困惑 , 沒有顏色的粒子 。
what this means is that , while regular acrylic only diffuses light around the edges , this one illuminates across the entire surface when i turn on the lights around it .	這個意思是 , 雖然規定的 , 雖然規則只會在邊緣邊緣的光線 , 這一塊幻燈片 , 當我在它周圍的光線上 。
two of the known applications for this material include interior design and multitouch systems .	為這個材料設計和模擬系統的其中之一 。
and thermochromic pigments change color at a given temperature .	而rmo染色移植顏色的顏色 。
so i'm going to place this on a hot plate that is set to a temperature only slightly higher than ambient and you can see what happens .	所以我要把它放在一個熱溫度上 , 就是為了一個溫度的溫度 , 你可以看到發生什麼事 。
so one of the principle applications for this material is , amongst other things , in baby bottles , so it indicates when the contents are cool enough to drink .	所以 , 其中一個原則應用在這個材料中 , 嬰兒還有其他東西 , 在嬰兒的瓶子中 , 發現 , 當內容很酷 。
so these are just a few of what are commonly known as smart materials .	所以這些只是少數人所謂的智慧材料 。
in a few years , they will be in many of the objects and technologies we use on a daily basis .	幾年後 , 他們會在許多物體和科技技術中使用 。
we may not yet have the flying cars science fiction promised us , but we can have walls that change color depending on temperature , keyboards that roll up , and windows that become opaque at the flick of a switch .	我們可能還沒有飛行科學效率 , 但我們能有牆壁上的牆壁 , 改變顏色依賴溫度、鍵盤、窗戶、窗戶、窗戶、窗戶、窗戶、窗戶、窗戶、窗戶的窗戶 。
so i'm a social scientist by training , so why am i here today talking about smart materials ?	我是一位訓練的社會科學家 , 所以我為什麼今天在這裡談論智慧材料 ?
well first of all , because i am a maker .	首先 , 因為我是個作家 。
i'm curious about how things work and how they are made , but also because i believe we should have a deeper understanding of the components that make up our world , and right now , we don't know enough about these hightech composites our future will be made of .	我很奇怪的是如何運作的 , 但也是因為我相信我們應該有更深刻了解這些複雜的元件 , 現在我們不知道這些高科技複雜的構造 , 現在我們不知道這些高科技的構造 。
smart materials are hard to obtain in small quantities .	智慧材料很難觀察到小量子裡 。
there's barely any information available on how to use them , and very little is said about how they are produced .	基本上有任何資訊可以用來使用它們的方式 , 而非常小的就是說他們如何生產 。
so for now , they exist mostly in this realm of trade secrets and patents only universities and corporations have access to .	所以現在 , 他們大部分的貿易秘密和專利只有大學和專利只能取得 。
so a little over three years ago , kirsty boyle and i started a project we called open materials .	三年前 , 肯定男孩們 , 我開始了一個計畫 , 我們稱之為開放材料 。
it's a website where we , and anyone else who wants to join us , share experiments , publish information , encourage others to contribute whenever they can , and aggregate resources such as research papers and tutorials by other makers like ourselves .	這是我們網站的網站 , 其他人想要加入我們 , 分享實驗、分享的資訊 , 鼓勵其他人 , 鼓勵其他人 , 鼓勵其他資源 , 比如研究紙和直覺的資源 , 比如研究紙和我們一樣 。
we would like it to become a large , collectively generated database of doityourself information on smart materials .	我們希望它成為一個大型、收集資料庫的資料庫 。
but why should we care how smart materials work and what they are made of ?	但我們為什麼要關心智慧材料如何運作 ?
first of all , because we can't shape what we don't understand , and what we don't understand and use ends up shaping us .	首先 , 因為我們無法理解的 , 而我們不了解、使用終結我們所不知道的 , 最後會把我們丟掉 。
the objects we use , the clothes we wear , the houses we live in , all have a profound impact on our behavior , health and quality of life .	我們使用、衣服、衣服、我們生活的房子裡都有很深刻影響我們的行為、健康和品質 。
so if we are to live in a world made of smart materials , we should know and understand them .	所以如果我們活在一個聰明的材料 , 我們應該知道它們 。
secondly , and just as important , innovation has always been fueled by tinkerers .	第二 , 創新的創新一直被燃燒了 。
so many times , amateurs , not experts , have been the inventors and improvers of things ranging from mountain bikes to semiconductors , personal computers , airplanes .	很多時候 , 護士 , 不是專家 , 而是發明家 , 而是來自山脈的生物 , 個人電腦、個人電腦、飛機、個人電腦、飛機、飛機、飛機、飛機 。
the biggest challenge is that material science is complex and requires expensive equipment .	最大的挑戰是 , 材料科學是複雜且需要昂貴的設備 。
but that's not always the case .	但這不是總是如此 。
two scientists at university of illinois understood this when they published a paper on a simpler method for making conductive ink .	兩位科學家在墨西哥大學發表了這篇文章 , 當他們發表了一篇簡單的方法 , 為了製造核心的文章 。
jordan bunker , who had had no experience with chemistry until then , read this paper and reproduced the experiment at his maker space using only offtheshelf substances and tools .	約翰布爾•布朗克斯 , 他沒有經歷過化學物質 , 閱讀這篇文章和工具 。
he used a toaster oven , and he even made his own vortex mixer , based on a tutorial by another scientist/maker .	他以前曾用一個東岸 , 他甚至做了自己的疫苗 , 根據另一位科學家/maker , 根據另一位科學家/maker 。
jordan then published his results online , including all the things he had tried and didn't work , so others could study and reproduce it .	約翰 , 接著發表了他的結果 , 包括他試驗的所有事情都沒有工作 , 所以其他人可以研究並複製它 。
so jordan's main form of innovation was to take an experiment created in a wellequipped lab at the university and recreate it in a garage in chicago using only cheap materials and tools he made himself .	所以約翰的主要形式是要把一個實驗在芝加哥大學中創造出來的實驗 , 在芝加哥大學裡 , 將它放在芝加哥大學裡 , 他讓自己更便宜的材料和工具 。
and now that he published this work , others can pick up where he left and devise even simpler processes and improvements .	現在他發表了這個作品 , 其他人可以把他左邊 , 其他簡單的過程 , 改善了甚至簡單的過程 。
another example i'd like to mention her project's goal is to highlight the expressive qualities of materials while focusing on the creativity and skills of the builder .	另一個例子我要提到她專案的目標是要高速的材料 , 雖然專注於創造力和技能的技能和技能 。
electronics kits are very powerful in that they teach us how things work , but the constraints inherent in their design influence the way we learn .	電子卡件非常強大 , 他們教導我們如何工作 , 但矛盾在他們的設計影響我們學習的方式 。
so hannah's approach , on the other hand , is to formulate a series of techniques for creating unusual objects that free us from predesigned constraints by teaching us about the materials themselves .	所以 , 漢娜的方法是 , 在另一方面 , 要形成一個獨特的物體 , 為我們創造獨立的物體 , 藉由教導我們自己的材料來源 。
so amongst hannah's many impressive experiments , this is one of my favorites .	所以 , 阿富汗有很多免疫實驗 , 這是我最喜歡的實驗之一之一 。
[ " paper speakers " ] what we're seeing here is just a piece of paper with some copper tape on it connected to an mp3 player and a magnet .	[報紙]我們看到的是 , 我們看到的是一張紙張和一些銅板上的紙張 , 和磁鐵連結在一起 , 和磁鐵連結在一起 。
so based on the research by marcelo coelho from mit , hannah created a series of paper speakers out of a wide range of materials from simple copper tape to conductive fabric and ink .	所以根據阿里斯的研究 , 來自麻省理工的研究 , 阿富汗創造了一系系列的材料 , 來自簡單的銅板和皮膚 。
just like jordan and so many other makers , hannah published her recipes and allows anyone to copy and reproduce them .	就像約翰和許多其他製造者一樣 , 漢娜發表了她的尊敬 , 允許任何人去複製它們 。
but paper electronics is one of the most promising branches of material science in that it allows us to create cheaper and flexible electronics .	但紙張是電子電子郵件之一 , 它讓我們能夠創造更便宜的材料科學 。
so hannah's artisanal work , and the fact that she shared her findings , opens the doors to a series of new possibilities that are both aesthetically appealing and innovative .	所以漢娜的藝術作品 , 她分享她的發現 , 她分享她的發現 , 開放了她的發現 , 開放了一系列新的可能性 。
so the interesting thing about makers is that we create out of passion and curiosity , and we are not afraid to fail .	所以 , 製造者有趣的事是 , 我們創造出熱情和好奇心 , 我們不是害怕失敗 。
we often tackle problems from unconventional angles , and , in the process , end up discovering alternatives or even better ways to do things .	我們經常從未預防角角角角度解決方案 , 在過程中 , 最終發現替代代方案或更好的方法 。
so the more people experiment with materials , the more researchers are willing to share their research , and manufacturers their knowledge , the better chances we have to create technologies that truly serve us all .	所以 , 更多研究者的實驗者 , 更多研究者會分享他們的知識 , 製造者的知識 , 更好的機會 , 我們必須創造技術 , 讓我們所有人都能創造技術 。
so i feel a bit as ted nelson must have when , in the early 1970s , he wrote , " you must understand computers now . "	所以我覺得有點像tednelon必須有時 , 在1970年代早期 , 他寫: 「 你現在必須了解電腦現在 」

so it's a little strange that i'm standing here and saying , " you must understand smart materials now . "	所以這有點奇怪 , 我站在這裡站在這裡說: 「 你必須了解智慧材料現在的智慧材料 。 」
just keep in mind that acquiring preemptive knowledge about emerging technologies is the best way to ensure that we have a say in the making of our future .	只要記住 , 就能保持這個技術 , 就能確保我們未來的最佳方法 , 確保我們有一個說法的方式來確保我們的未來 。
when we drive , we get into a glass bubble , lock the doors and press the accelerator , relying on our eyes to guide us even though we can only see the few cars ahead of and behind us . but what if cars could share data with each other about their position and velocity , and use predictive models to calculate the safest routes for everyone on the road ? jennifer healey imagines a world without accidents .	當我們開車時 , 我們進入了一個玻璃泡 , 鎖住門和壓縮器 , 通常在我們的眼睛上 , 甚至在我們眼前看到一些車輛 , 但如果汽車可以跟我們分享資料分享資料 。 但如果卡車可以與其他人分享他們的位置 , 來預測他們的位置 , 利用模型 , 來預測每個人 。
jennifer healey: if cars could talk , accidents might be avoidable	珍妮•亨利:如果汽車能說話 , 意外可能是避免的 。
let's face it: driving is dangerous .	讓我們面對它:開車是危險的 。

car accidents are the leading cause of death in people ages 16 to 19 in the united states leading cause of death and 75 percent of these accidents have nothing to do with drugs or alcohol .	根據美國人的領導人是16歲到19歲的死亡導致死亡和75%的疾病導致死亡率和75% 。
no one can say for sure , but i remember my first accident .	沒有人能說清楚 , 但我記得我的第一個準確 。

i'm like , " okay , all right , this guy is slowing down , i'll slow down too . "	我說: 「 好吧 , 好吧 , 這傢伙慢下來了 , 我會慢下來 。 」

but i had no idea that car was stopping , and i think we can do a lot better than that .	但我不知道汽車正在停止 , 我認為我們可以做得更好 。
i think we can transform the driving experience by letting our cars talk to each other .	我認為我們可以改變車禍的經驗 , 讓車子和彼此溝通 。
i just want you to think a little bit about what the experience of driving is like now .	我想你們稍稍稍微思考一下 , 開車的經驗 。
get into your car . close the door . you're in a glass bubble .	拿到你的車子裡 , 你在一個玻璃泡裡 。
you can't really directly sense the world around you .	你看不到你周圍的世界 。
you're in this extended body .	你在這個獨立的身體 。

okay ? and all you have to guide you are your two eyes .	好嗎 ? 各位必須猜你是兩個眼睛 。
okay , so that's all you have , eyes that weren't really designed for this task , but then people ask you to do things like , you want to make a lane change , what's the first thing they ask you do ?	好吧 , 這就是你所擁有的眼睛 , 但當人們要求你做的事 , 但當人們問你 , 你想要做些什麼事 ?
take your eyes off the road . that's right .	把你的眼睛放下來 , 這是對的 。
stop looking where you're going , turn , check your blind spot , and drive down the road without looking where you're going .	停止看看你在哪裡 , 看看你在哪裡 , 把你的盲點放在哪裡 。

why do we do this ? because we have to , we have to make a choice , do i look here or do i look here ?	為什麼我們要這樣做 ? 因為我們必須做出選擇 , 我看看這裡 , 或者我看這裡 ?

in the future , with cars exchanging data with each other , we will be able to see not just three cars ahead and three cars behind , to the right and left , all at the same time , bird's eye view , we will actually be able to see into those cars .	在未來 , 車子裡 , 有車外的資料 , 我們就能看到不只是三輛車、三輛車、左邊、左邊、鳥類的眼睛看法 , 我們就能看到這些車子 。

and with computation and algorithms and predictive models , we will be able to see the future .	計算和演算法和演算法模型 , 我們就能看見未來 。

how can you predict the future ? that's really hard .	你要如何預測未來 ? 那真的很難 。
actually , no . with cars , it's not impossible .	事實上 , 沒有車子 , 沒有 。
cars are threedimensional objects that have a fixed position and velocity .	車子是三維度的物體 , 車子是三維度的物體 。
they travel down roads .	他們走下路路 。
often they travel on prepublished routes .	通常他們在懷孕的路上旅行 。
it's really not that hard to make reasonable predictions about where a car's going to be in the near future .	這並不難以做出理想的預測 , 車子將會在近未來 。
even if , when you're in your car and some motorcyclist comes bshoom ! 85 miles an hour down , lanesplitting i know you've had this experience that guy didn't " just come out of nowhere . "	即使是 , 當你在車裡 , 一些動作家 , 有些動作家 ! 85英哩 , 雷射我知道你們有這個經驗 , 不只發生在哪裡 。 」
that guy's been on the road probably for the last half hour .	那個傢伙已經在過去一半小時 。
right ? i mean , somebody's seen him .	對嗎 ? 我的意思是 , 有人看過他 。
ten , 20 , 30 miles back , someone's seen that guy , and as soon as one car sees that guy and puts him on the map , he's on the map position , velocity , good estimate he'll continue going 85 miles an hour .	20、20、30英哩背後 , 有人看過那個傢伙 , 一輛汽車看到地圖 , 把他放在地圖上 , 他會繼續下85英哩 。
you'll know , because your car will know , because that other car will have whispered something in his ear , like , " by the way , five minutes , motorcyclist , watch out . "	你知道的 , 因為你的車子會知道 , 因為其他車子會在他的耳朵裡 , 比如: 「 五分鐘、五分鐘、動機學家 , 看看 。 」

i mean , they're newtonian objects .	我的意思是 , 他們是新客觀的 。
that's very nice about them .	這對他們來說很棒 。
so how do we get there ?	所以 , 我們要如何做到呢 ?
we can start with something as simple as sharing our position data between cars , just sharing gps .	我們可以從車子開始 , 車子之間分享我們的位置 , 只是分享gpps 。
if i have a gps and a camera in my car , i have a pretty precise idea of where i am and how fast i'm going .	如果我有一個gpps和a攝影機 , 我有一個非常精確的想法 , 我有多快 。
with computer vision , i can estimate where the cars around me are , sort of , and where they're going .	有電腦視覺 , 我可以估計我周圍的車輛 , 可以估計 。
and same with the other cars .	另一輛車一樣 。
they can have a precise idea of where they are , and sort of a vague idea of where the other cars are .	他們能擁有一個精確的想法 , 有點像是其他車子的概念 。
what happens if two cars share that data , if they talk to each other ?	如果兩輛車共享資料 , 如果他們跟彼此溝通 ?
i can tell you exactly what happens .	我可以告訴你發生什麼事 。
professor bob wang and his team have done computer simulations of what happens when fuzzy estimates combine , even in light traffic , when cars just share gps data , and we've moved this research out of the computer simulation and into robot test beds that have the actual sensors that are in cars now on these robots: stereo cameras , gps , and the twodimensional laser range finders that are common in backup systems .	專業炸彈和他的團隊做了電腦模擬時發生了什麼事 , 甚至在光線上 , 甚至在光線上分享gptfic , 我們搬到電腦模擬電腦模擬電腦模擬電腦模擬器 , 並進入機器人測驗機械測驗器中 , 我們將這兩台機器的模擬器官 。
we also attach a discrete shortrange communication radio , and the robots talk to each other .	我們也在沙灘溝通輻射溝通輻射溝通 , 而機器人和機器人交談 。
when these robots come at each other , they track each other's position precisely , and they can avoid each other .	當這些機器人來到彼此時 , 他們追蹤彼此追蹤彼此的位置 , 他們可以避免彼此避免 。
we're now adding more and more robots into the mix , and we encountered some problems .	現在我們現在加上更多機器人進入混合 , 我們遇到一些問題 。
one of the problems , when you get too much chatter , it's hard to process all the packets , so you have to prioritize , and that's where the predictive model helps you .	問題是 , 當你得到太多的章魚 , 很難處理所有包裝 , 所以你必須把所有包裝起來 , 這就是預測模式幫助你 。
if your robot cars are all tracking the predicted trajectories , you don't pay as much attention to those packets .	如果你的機器人都在追蹤軌道上追蹤軌道 , 你不會注意到這些頁面 。
you prioritize the one guy who seems to be going a little off course .	你把其中一個人放下來 , 似乎有點不錯 。
that guy could be a problem .	這傢伙可能是個問題 。
and you can predict the new trajectory .	你可以預測新的軌道 。
so you don't only know that he's going off course , you know how .	所以 , 你不只知道他會走下去 。
and you know which drivers you need to alert to get out of the way .	你知道 , 驅動者需要更活躍 。
and we wanted to do how can we best alert everyone ?	我們想要怎麼做才能更好的酒吧 ?
how can these cars whisper , " you need to get out of the way ? "	這些卡車是怎麼辦 ? " 你需要從哪裡來 ? "
well , it depends on two things: one , the ability of the car , and second the ability of the driver .	嗯 , 它依賴兩件事:第一 , 汽車的能力 , 第二 , 駕駛者的能力 。
if one guy has a really great car , but they're on their phone or , you know , doing something , they're not probably in the best position to react in an emergency .	如果一個人有很棒的車子 , 但他們在手機上做些什麼 , 做些事 , 他們不可能在最好的位置 。
so we started a separate line of research doing driver state modeling .	所以我們開始了一個研究司機模型 。
and now , using a series of three cameras , we can detect if a driver is looking forward , looking away , looking down , on the phone , or having a cup of coffee .	現在 , 使用一系列三張攝影師 , 我們可以偵測到手機 , 看看 , 看看 , 看看 , 在手機上 , 或是有一杯咖啡杯咖啡 。
we can predict the accident and we can predict who , which cars , are in the best position to move out of the way to calculate the safest route for everyone .	我們可以預測誰 , 我們可以預測誰 , 汽車、最好的位置 , 最好的位置 , 來計算每個人的最佳位置 。
fundamentally , these technologies exist today .	基本上 , 這些技術存在今天 。
i think the biggest problem that we face is our own willingness to share our data .	我認為我們面臨最大的問題是 , 我們自己的資料 。
i think it's a very disconcerting notion , this idea that our cars will be watching us , talking about us to other cars , that we'll be going down the road in a sea of gossip .	我認為這是一件非常令人沮喪的概念 , 我們的車子將會看著使用其他車輛 , 談論我們 , 談論我們 , 談論我們 , 我們將要走到另一輛車上 。
but i believe it can be done in a way that protects our privacy , just like right now , when i look at your car from the outside , i don't really know about you .	但我相信它可以保護我們的隱私 , 就像現在一樣 , 當我從外面看你的車輛 , 我不知道你們的車輛 。
if i look at your license plate number , i don't really know who you are .	如果我看看你的謊言數字 , 我不知道你是誰 。
i believe our cars can talk about us behind our backs .	我相信我們的車子可以談論我們背後的車子 。
and i think it's going to be a great thing .	我認為這將會是個很棒的事 。
i want you to consider for a moment if you really don't want the distracted teenager behind you to know that you're braking , that you're coming to a dead stop .	我想請各位考慮一下如果你真的不想把青少年隔離的青少年你知道你正在勇敢的停止 。
by sharing our data willingly , we can do what's best for everyone .	透過分享我們的資料將會做到最好的 , 我們可以做些什麼 。
so let your car gossip about you .	所以 , 咱們來看看你們 。
it's going to make the roads a lot safer .	它會讓道路變得更安全 。

i'm a medical illustrator , and i come from a slightly different point of view .	我是個醫師 , 我是來自一個非常不同的觀點 。
i've been watching , since i grew up , the expressions of truth and beauty in the arts and truth and beauty in the sciences .	我一直在看著藝術和美麗的表情和美麗的表情和真相的表情 。
and while these are both wonderful things in their own right they both have very wonderful things going for them truth and beauty as ideals that can be looked at by the sciences and by math are almost like the ideal conjoined twins that a scientist would want to date .	雖然這些都是很棒的事 , 他們兩者都有很棒的事 , 她們兩者都很美妙的事情 , 數學是科學和美麗的小鎮 , 幾乎像lojoinedinedinedinedinedinedinedindin 。
these are expressions of truth as awefull things , by meaning they are things you can worship .	這些都是真理的事物 , 意思是 , 它們是你能擔心的東西 。
they are ideals that are powerful . they are irreducible .	他們是理想的 , 他們是很有力的 。
they are unique . they are useful sometimes , often a long time after the fact .	他們很獨特 , 他們有時候很有用 , 通常在事實上 。
and you can actually roll some of the pictures now , because i don't want to look at me on the screen .	實際上你可以現在一些照片 , 因為我不想看看螢幕上我 。
truth and beauty are things that are often opaque to people who are not in the sciences .	真相和美麗的是 , 常常常見的事物 。
they are things that describe beauty in a way that is often only accessible if you understand the language and the syntax of the person who studies the subject in which truth and beauty is expressed .	他們在某種程度上描述的美麗 , 通常只有你了解語言和美麗的組合 , 如果你了解語言和美麗的組合 。
if you look at the math , e=mc squared , if you look at the cosmological constant , where there's an anthropic ideal , where you see that life had to evolve from the numbers that describe the universe these are things that are really difficult to understand .	如果你看數學、e=mccc=mcccared , 如果你看看宇宙的宇宙中 , 你可以看到生命必須從哪裡來演化的數字 , 你可以看到生命必須從哪裡來演化 。
and what i've tried to do since i had my training as a medical illustrator since i was taught animation by my father , who was a sculptor and my visual mentor i wanted to figure out a way to help people understand truth and beauty in the biological sciences by using animation , by using pictures , by telling stories so that the things that are not necessarily evident to people can be brought forth , and can be taught , and can be understood .	我從我教導我的訓練作為醫師 , 從我父親教導我 , 由我父親教導我 , 他是個雕塑家和美麗的男人 , 我想要找出一個方法來協助人們了解真相和美麗的生物科學 , 透過圖像來幫助人們了解真相 , 透過照片來了解真相和美麗的事物 。
students today are often immersed in an environment where what they learn is subjects that have truth and beauty embedded in them , but the way they're taught is compartmentalized and it's drawn down to the point where the truth and beauty are not always evident .	現今 , 學生通常在一個環境中 , 他們學到的是真相和美麗和美麗的環境 , 但他們教導的方式是比較複雜的 , 但他們教導真相和美麗 。
it's almost like that old recipe for chicken soup where you boil the chicken until the flavor is just gone .	這幾乎就像那隻老鼠一樣的老鼠 , 直到你買雞肉 , 直到衝突只是消失了 。
we don't want to do that to our students .	我們不想做這件事 。
so we have an opportunity to really open up education .	所以我們有機會開放教育 。
and i had a telephone call from robert lue at harvard , in the molecular and cellular biology department , a couple of years ago . he asked me if my team and i would be interested and willing to really change how medical and scientific education is done at harvard .	我有一個電話來自哈佛大學的電話電話電話 , 幾年前 , 分子和細胞生物學辯論 , 幾年前 , 他問我 , 如果我的團隊和我有興趣 , 我會很感興趣 , 他問我 , 如果我的團隊和科學教育教育教育是在哈佛大學的 。
so we embarked on a project that would explore the cell that would explore the truth and beauty inherent in molecular and cellular biology so that students could understand a larger picture that they could hang all of these facts on .	所以我們在一個專案上 , 會探索真相和美麗的細胞 , 來探索真相和細胞生物學 , 學生可以理解一個更大的照片 。

these micromachines , which are the envy of nanotechnologists the world over , are selfdirected , powerful , precise , accurate devices that are made out of strings of amino acids .	這些微生物學家 , 這是世界各地的感官 , 是自動化、強大、強大、強大、強大、精確、精確、精確、精確的設備 。

and so what we wanted to do was to figure out how we could make this story into an animation that would be the centerpiece of biovisions at harvard , which is a website that harvard has for its molecular and cellular biology students that will in addition to all the textual information , in addition to all the didactic stuff put everything together visually , so that these students would have an internalized view of what a cell really is in all of its truth and beauty , and be able to study with this view in mind , so that their imaginations would be sparked , so that their passions would be sparked and so that they would be able to go on and use these visions in their head to make new discoveries and to be able to find out , really , how life works .	所以我們想做的是 , 找出我們要如何讓這個故事成為一個模擬的中心源頭 , 將是哈佛大學的網站 , 這是哈佛和細胞生物學所需要的分子和細胞生物學相關資訊 , 加上了所有的文字 , 加上所有的文字 , 加上了所有東西 , 都能把這些東西放在一起 。

we worked with a theme , which is , you've got macrophages that are streaming down a capillary , and they're touching the surface of the capillary wall , and they're picking up information from cells that are on the capillary wall , and they are given this information that there's an inflammation somewhere outside , where they can't see and sense .	我們和一個味道合作 , 就是 , 你有麥克風的表面 , 牠們正在追蹤捕捕捉水面的表面 , 牠們會從小牆面上拿出來的資訊 , 牠們把這些資訊從外面看不到 。
but they get the information that causes them to stop , causes them to internalize that they need to make all of the various parts that will cause them to change their shape , and try to get out of this capillary and find out what's going on .	但他們得到的資訊 , 讓他們停止 , 使他們能夠改變它們的形狀 , 讓他們改變它們的形狀 , 試著找出這些船隻的樣子 , 試著找出什麼會發生什麼事 。

but these machines that power the inside of the cells are really quite amazing , and they really are the basis of all life because all of these machines interact with each other .	但這些機器內部的力量非常令人驚訝 , 他們真的是所有這些機器互動的基礎 , 因為所有這些機器和彼此互動 。

becky blanton planned to live in her van for a year and see the country , but when depression set in and her freelance job ended , her camping trip turned into homelessness . in this intimate talk , she describes her experience of becoming one of america's working homeless .	貝洛頓計畫要活在她的優勢中 , 看看國家 , 但當憂鬱設置和自由工作結束時 , 她的營養工作結束時 , 她的營運 , 她在這個演講中 , 她描述她描述了一家美國的經驗之一 。
adventure , happiness , life , personal growth , poverty , social change , society , storytelling	冒險、幸福、生命、個人成長、貧窮、社會改變、社會、貧窮、社會改變、社會、故事 。
becky blanton: the year i was homeless	貝爾•布頓:一年我很無家 。
i'm a writer and a journalist , and i'm also an insanely curious person , so in 22 years as a journalist , i've learned how to do a lot of new things .	我是個作家和記者 , 我也是個很奇妙的人 , 所以在22年後 , 我也學到了很多新的事物 。
and three years ago , one of the things i learned how to do was to become invisible .	三年前 , 我學到要怎麼做才能成為不可能的 。
i became one of the working homeless .	我成為工作的一家工作之一 。
i quit my job as a newspaper editor after my father died in february of that same year , and decided to travel .	我把工作當作報告當作報告後 , 我父親在那一年之後 , 決定去旅行 。
his death hit me pretty hard .	他的死亡讓我非常困難 。
and there were a lot of things that i wanted to feel and deal with while i was doing that .	我想要感受到很多事情 , 我在做這件事 。
i've camped my whole life . and i decided that living in a van for a year to do this would be like one long camping trip .	我把我的整個人生中 , 我決定在一年內 , 我決定住在一個很長的試驗 。
so i packed my cat , my rottweiler and my camping gear into a 1975 chevy van , and drove off into the sunset , having fully failed to realize three critical things .	所以 , 我把我的貓帶到1975年 , 我在開車上跑到1975年 , 開進了太陽能板上升到太陽能上三種關鍵的事情 。
one: that society equates living in a permanent structure , even a shack , with having value as a person .	第一:那社會和平等結構 , 即使有價值觀 , 甚至有價值觀 。
two: i failed to realize how quickly the negative perceptions of other people can impact our reality , if we let it .	第二:我無法了解別人的負面感知 , 如果我們讓它影響我們的現實 , 如果我們讓它影響我們的現實 。
three: i failed to realize that homelessness is an attitude , not a lifestyle .	第三:我無法意識到 , 無家可歸是態度 , 而不是生命典型的 。
at first , living in the van was great .	首先 , 住在梵谷裡 。
i showered in campgrounds . i ate out regularly .	我在咖啡廳裡展示了很多 。
and i had time to relax and to grieve .	我必須重新拒絕和悲傷 。
but then the anger and the depression about my father's death set in .	但之後憤怒和憂鬱症的憂鬱症 。
my freelance job ended . and i had to get a fulltime job to pay the bills .	我的自由工作結束了 , 我必須得到一份工作 , 要付出一份工作 。
what had been a really mild spring turned into a miserably hot summer .	什麼是一英哩春天的春天 。
and it became impossible to park anywhere without being very obvious that i had a cat and a dog with me , and it was really hot .	而且它變得不可能公園 , 沒有太明顯我有貓和狗狗一起狗狗狗狗狗狗狗狗狗狗狗狗狗
the cat came and went through an open window in the van .	貓走來 , 穿過一個開放窗戶 。
the doggy went into doggy day care .	卵子進入蛋白天照顧 。
whenever i could , i used employee showers in office buildings and truck stops .	儘管我可以在辦公室裡 , 我在辦公室裡 , 卡車停下來 。
or i washed up in public rest rooms .	或者我在公共餐廳裡 。
nighttime temperatures in the van rarely dropped below 80 degrees fahrenheit , making it difficult or impossible to sleep .	晚上溫度降低80度的溫度降低80度的信仰 , 讓它睡眠變得困難或不可能睡眠 。
food rotted in the heat .	食物把熱帶放在熱水中 。
ice in my ice chest melted within hours , and it was pretty miserable .	我在幾小時內冰箱裡收到的冰箱裡 , 很糟糕 。
i couldn't afford to find an apartment , or couldn't afford an apartment that would allow me to have the rottweiler and the cat .	我無法承認一個公寓 , 還是無法負擔公寓 , 不舒服的公寓 , 以及貓咪 。
and i refused to give them up , so i stayed in the van .	我拒絕給他們 , 所以我拒絕給他們 。
and when the heat made me too sick to walk the 50 feet to the public restroom outside my van at night , i used a bucket and a trash bag as a toilet .	當熱熱帶帶給我太生病時 , 我晚上走了五英呎的公共餐廳 , 我用一桶麵包和垃圾桶一樣 。
when winter weather set in , the temperatures dropped below freezing . and they stayed there .	當冬天的溫度時 , 溫度降低了 , 溫度就在那邊 。 他們留在那裡 。
and i faced a whole new set of challenges .	我面對了一個全新的挑戰 。
i parked a different place every night so i would avoid being noticed and hassled by the police .	我每天晚上找了不同的地方 , 所以我會避免警察 。
i didn't always succeed .	我不總是成功 。
but i felt out of control of my life .	但我感受到我的人生中 。
and i don't know when or how it happened , but the speed at which i went from being a talented writer and journalist to being a homeless woman , living in a van , took my breath away .	我不知道它發生了什麼事 , 但在那時候我從一個小寫作家和記者成為一個無家的女子 , 帶著我的呼吸 , 帶著我的呼吸 。
i hadn't changed . my i . q . hadn't dropped .	我沒有改變了 。 我 , q..
my talent , my integrity , my values , everything about me remained the same .	我的財富、我的價值觀、價值、價值、價值、所有關於記憶的一切 。
but i had changed somehow .	但我改變了一些 。
i spiraled deeper and deeper into a depression .	我精神深深深深深入的憂鬱症 。
and eventually someone referred me to a homeless health clinic .	最終 , 有人拒絕我回到一個無家的健康診所 。
and i went . i hadn't bathed in three days .	我去了 , 我沒有在三天內 。
i was as smelly and as depressed as anyone in line .	我很孤獨 , 身為任何人感到沮喪 。
i just wasn't drunk or high .	我不只是喝醉或高度 。
and when several of the homeless men realized that , including a former university professor , they said , " you aren't homeless . why are you really here ? "	當無家的數人意識到 , 包括一個形式大學教授時 , 他們說: 「 你不是家人 。 」
other homeless people didn't see me as homeless , but i did .	其他無家人看不到我 , 但我做了 。
then the professor listened to my story and he said , " you have a job . you have hope .	接著 , 專業傾聽我的故事 , 他說: 「 你有一個工作 。 你有希望 。 」
the real homeless don't have hope . "	真正的家人沒有希望 。 」
a reaction to the medication the clinic gave me for my depression left me suicidal . and i remember thinking , " if i killed myself , no one would notice . "	醫學給我憂鬱症患者的反應讓我感到憂鬱 , 我記得: 「 如果我殺死自己 , 沒有人會注意到: 「 如果我殺了自己 , 沒有人注意到 。 」
a friend told me , shortly after that , that she had heard that tim russert , a nationally renowned journalist , had been talking about me on national t . v .	一位朋友告訴我 , 她聽說 , 她聽過最短的記者 , 一個全國記者 , 全國新聞記者 , 一直在談論我國家的報導 。
an essay i'd written about my father , the year before he died , was in tim's new book .	我寫了我父親寫了關於我父親的那一年 , 在他死後 , 他在tim是新書的 。
