author and activist isabel allende discusses women , creativity , the definition of feminism and , of course , passion in this talk .	身為女性和活動者是阿拉伯女性、創意、創意、創意、創意、創意、有熱情的定義 。
entertainment , global issues , love , parenting , storytelling , women , world cultures	娛樂、全球議題、愛、父母、公寓、女人、女人、世界文化、世界文化、文化、文化 。
isabel allende tells tales of passion	伊莎貝爾所有會說的熱情 。
thank you so much . it's really scary to be here among the smartest of the smart .	非常謝各位 , 真的很害怕 , 這裡是聰明的 。
i'm here to tell you a few tales of passion .	我要告訴各位一些熱情的熱情 。
there's a jewish saying that i love .	有一個猶太人說我愛 。
what is truer than truth ? answer: the story .	什麼比真相呢 ? 答案:故事 。
i'm a storyteller . i want to convey something that is truer than truth about our common humanity .	我是個故事者 , 我想讓大家分享一些事情比我們共同的人類性 。
all stories interest me , and some haunt me until i end up writing them .	所有故事都有興趣 , 直到我最後寫了這些故事 。
certain themes keep coming up: justice , loyalty , violence , death , political and social issues , freedom .	某些人繼續上升:正義、暴力、政治、政治、社會議題、自由、社會議題、自由、自由 。
i'm aware of the mystery around us , so i write about coincidences , premonitions , emotions , dreams , the power of nature , magic .	我對我們周圍的謎團 , 所以我寫關於宇宙、情緒、情緒、情緒、夢想、夢想、魔術、魔術、魔術、魔術、魔術、魔術、魔術、魔術 。
in the last 20 years i have published a few books , but i have lived in anonymity until february of 2006 , when i carried the olympic flag in the winter olympics in italy .	在過去二十年 , 我已經發表了一些書 , 但我住在2006年 , 直到2006年 , 當我把奧運送到冬季時 , 我在義大利奧地地地跳進去 。
that made me a celebrity . now people recognize me in macy's , and my grandchildren think that i'm cool .	這讓我感到慶祝 。 現在人們認同我在數學上認知我很酷 。
allow me to tell you about my four minutes of fame .	讓我告訴各位我的四分鐘 。
one of the organizers of the olympic ceremony , of the opening ceremony , called me and said that i had been selected to be one of the flagbearers .	氧氣中的其中之一之一 , 開放酵素之一 , 打開冰球 , 叫我 , 說我一直被選為旗幟之一 。
i replied that surely this was a case of mistaken identity because i'm as far as you can get from being an athlete .	我相信這是個錯誤的案例 , 因為我身為你所能從一個青少年開始 。
actually , i wasn't even sure that i could go around the stadium without a walker .	事實上 , 我甚至不確定我可以走到樓梯裡 , 沒有走路 。
i was told that this was no laughing matter .	我告訴這不是笑話 。
this would be the first time that only women would carry the olympic flag .	這是第一次 , 只有女性會帶著奧運旗幟 。
five women , representing five continents , and three olympic gold medal winners .	五個女性 , 代表五個大陸的黃金金 , 三種奧運的金屬贏家 。
my first question was , naturally , what was i going to wear ?	我第一個問題是 , 天然地 , 我要穿什麼 ?
a uniform , she said , and asked for my measurements .	她說 , 她說: 「 衡量我的測量 。 」
i had a vision of myself in a fluffy anorak , looking like the michelin man .	我有一扇門的願景 , 就像我一樣 。
by the middle of february , i found myself in turin , where enthusiastic crowds cheered when any of the 80 olympic teams was in the street .	透過佛羅斯的中間 , 我發現自己在沙漠中發現自己在街坊中找到自己 。
those athletes had sacrificed everything to compete in the games .	那些青少年有平靜的一切都要競爭 。
they all deserved to win , but there's the element of luck .	他們都要贏 , 但還有幸運的元素 。
a speck of snow , an inch of ice , the force of the wind , can determine the result of a race or a game .	一個冰層的速度 , 一個冰川的力量 , 可以決定種族或遊戲 。
however , what matters most more than training or luck is the heart .	然而 , 最重要的是訓練或幸運是心臟 。
only a fearless and determined heart will get the gold medal .	只有一種無害且決定心臟會得到黃金 。
it is all about passion .	這是關於熱情 。
the streets of turin were covered with red posters announcing the slogan of the olympics .	皮膚的街道是紅色郵件的街道 。
passion lives here . isn't it always true ?	熱情生活 , 不是真的嗎 ?
heart is what drives us and determines our fate .	心臟是驅動我們和決策 。
that is what i need for my characters in my books: a passionate heart .	這就是我書中需要我的角色:一個熱情心 。
i need mavericks , dissidents , adventurers , outsiders and rebels , who ask questions , bend the rules and take risks .	我需要麥克、分散、外科醫生、外科醫生、外科醫生 , 問問問題: 「 規則和冒險 。 」
people like all of you in this room .	像你們一樣都在這個房間裡 。
nice people with common sense do not make interesting characters .	很棒的人 , 不讓有趣的角色變得很有趣 。
they only make good former spouses .	他們只製造更好的形式 。
in the green room of the stadium , i met the other flag bearers: three athletes , and the actresses susan sarandon and sophia loren .	在壓力中 , 我遇到其他旗幟的綠色房間裡 , 另外一個旗幟:三分之一的運動員 。
also , two women with passionate hearts: wangari maathai , the nobel prizewinner from kenya who has planted 30 million trees . and by doing so , she has changed the soil , the weather , in some places in africa , and of course the economic conditions in many villages .	同時 , 兩位婦女熱情心:哇 , 諾貝爾獎獎 , 她從肯亞到肯亞 , 她已經改變了土壤 , 她改變了土壤 , 當然 , 她改變了土壤 , 當然 , 她改變了土壤 , 當然經濟條件 。
and somaly mam , a cambodian activist who fights passionately against child prostitution .	所以 , 馬上 , 一位柬埔寨活動家 , 他對抗孩子的熱情 。
when she was 14 years old , her grandfather sold her to a brothel .	當她14歲的時候 , 她祖父告訴我她祖父 。
she told us of little girls raped by men who believe that having sex with a very young virgin will cure them from aids .	她告訴我們一些小女孩 , 相信和一個非常年輕的村莊會將她們從愛滋病來治癒他們 。
and of brothels where children are forced to receive five , 15 clients per day , and if they rebel , they are tortured with electricity .	兄弟每天被迫害5 , 15個客戶每天都被迫害 , 15個客戶 , 如果他們拒絕 , 他們就會和電力 。
in the green room i received my uniform .	在綠色房間裡 , 我接受了我的平台 。
it was not the kind of outfit that i normally wear , but it was far from the michelin man suit that i had anticipated . not bad , really .	這不是我常常穿過的 , 而是從michennnman成功 , 但它是從michennnman , 真的 。
i looked like a refrigerator .	我看起來像一家咖啡師 。
but so did most of the flagbearers , except sophia loren , the universal symbol of beauty and passion .	但很多旗幟 , 大部分的旗幟 , 除了美麗和熱情有關的美麗和熱情 。
sophia is over 70 and she looks great .	細菌超過70歲 , 她看起來很棒 。
she's sexy , slim and tall , with a deep tan .	她是性戀、貧民和尾巴 , 帶著深蒂固 。
now , how can you have a deep tan and have no wrinkles ?	現在 , 你要如何擁有深密密碼 , 沒有寫字 ?
when asked in a tv interview , " how could she look so good ? "	當邀請電視訪問時 , 「 她怎麼看得很好 ? 」
she replied , " posture . my back is always straight , and i don't make old people's noises . "	她複製了: 「 海報 , 我的背後總是很明顯 , 我不讓老人沒有噪音 。 」
so , there you have some free advice from one of the most beautiful women on earth .	所以 , 有一些免費來自地球上最美麗的女性 。
no grunting , no coughing , no wheezing , no talking to yourselves , no farting .	不幸的是 , 沒有教導 , 不論你的elvetve , 不用擔心你的elve , 沒有農場 。
well , she didn't say that exactly .	嗯 , 她沒有這麼說 。
at some point around midnight , we were summoned to the wings of the stadium , and the loudspeakers announced the olympic flag , and the music started by the way , the same music that starts here , the aida march .	在某個時候 , 我們突然突然間 , 我們突然突然突然間 , 奧克•彼得•彼得•帕克•帕克•帕克•帕克•帕克•帕克•帕特 , 音樂從這裡開始 , 這裡開始 , 愛滋病毒開始 。
sophia loren was right in front of me she's a foot taller than i am , not counting the poofy hair .	在我面前 , 她比我前面 , 比我還要高 , 不是在我面前 , 而不是在池塘裡 。
she walked elegantly , like a giraffe on the african savannah , holding the flag on her shoulder . i jogged behind on my tiptoes holding the flag on my extended arm , so that my head was actually under the damn flag .	她走路很大 , 就像非洲沙漠一樣 , 把旗子放在她的肩膀上 , 把旗子放在我的手臂上 。 我腦袋裡的旗幟上 , 所以我的頭部其實在丹佛旗幟上 。
all the cameras were , of course , on sophia .	當然 , 所有的攝影機都是如此 。
that was fortunate for me , because in most press photos i appear too , although often between sophia's legs .	對我來說 , 這對我來說很幸運的是 , 雖然大部分的媒體拍照 , 雖然在蘇西亞的法律 。
a place where most men would love to be .	大部分男人會喜歡蜜蜂的地方 。
the best four minutes of my entire life were those in the olympic stadium .	我整個人生中最好的四分鐘 , 就是那些在奧運店裡 。
my husband is offended when i say this although i have explained to him that what we do in private usually takes less than four minutes so he shouldn't take it personally .	我丈夫被告知當我說這件事時 , 我必須向他解釋我們在私人身上做的事 , 通常不需要四分鐘的時間 。
i have all the press clippings of those four magnificent minutes , because i don't want to forget them when old age destroys my brain cells .	我有所有的憂鬱症 , 每四個偉大的壓力 , 因為我不想忘記他們腦細胞 。
i want to carry in my heart forever the key word of the olympics passion .	我想帶著我的心臟 , 儘管我心臟熱情的關鍵詞 。
so here's a tale of passion .	這就是熱情的熱情 。
the year is 1998 , the place is a prison camp for tutsi refugees in congo .	今年是1998年 , 地方是監獄難民營的難民營 。
by the way , 80 percent of all refugees and displaced people in the world are women and girls .	順便一提 , 世界上80%的難民和女孩 。
we can call this place in congo a death camp , because those who are not killed will die of disease or starvation .	我們可以稱之為死亡營養營 , 因為那些沒有殺死疾病或飢餓 。
the protagonists of this story are a young woman , rose mapendo , and her children .	這個故事是一位年輕女性、羅馬、羅馬、羅馬、她的孩子 。
she's pregnant and a widow .	她懷孕 , 一隻翅膀 。
soldiers have forced her to watch as her husband was tortured and killed .	士兵們被迫害她視為她的丈夫 , 殺死了 。
somehow she manages to keep her seven children alive , and a few months later , she gives birth to premature twins .	她可以保持她七個孩子活著 , 幾個月後 , 幾個月後 , 她給她的兄弟 。
two tiny little boys .	兩個小男孩 。
she cuts the umbilical cord with a stick , and ties it with her own hair .	她把腫瘤切割切割掉 , 用她自己的頭髮 , 用她自己的頭髮 。
she names the twins after the camp's commanders to gain their favor , and feeds them with black tea because her milk cannot sustain them .	她稱之為 「 貓咪 」 之後 , 她把他們的重力帶到他們的重力 , 餵飽黑茶 , 因為她的牛奶無法保持它們 。
when the soldiers burst in her cell to rape her oldest daughter , she grabs hold of her and refuses to let go , even when they hold a gun to her head .	當士兵在她的細胞裡燒掉她最老的女兒 , 她抓住她 , 抓住她的頭髮 , 即使他們拿著槍枝 。
somehow , the family survives for 16 months , and then , by extraordinary luck , and the passionate heart of a young american man , sasha chanoff , who manages to put her in a u . s . rescue plane , rose mapendo and her nine children end up in phoenix , arizona , where they're now living and thriving .	有些時候 , 家庭存活了16個月 , 接著 , 藉由很不凡的幸運 , 然後 , 一位年輕人 , 阿哈諾夫的熱情 , 他可以把她放進美國人放進美國的地圖 , 羅斯和她的九個孩子們結婚 。
mapendo , in swahili , means great love .	地圖 , 在波利亞 , 意味著好愛 。
the protagonists of my books are strong and passionate women like rose mapendo .	我的書籍是強烈且熱情的女性 , 比如羅馬圖圖書館 。
i don't make them up . there's no need for that .	我不讓它們放棄 。 我不需要這麼做 。
i look around and i see them everywhere .	我看著他們周圍 , 我看到他們 。
i have worked with women and for women all my life .	我和婦女和女性一起工作 。
i know them well .	我知道他們 。
i was born in ancient times , at the end of the world , in a patriarchal catholic and conservative family .	我出生於古老的時代 , 在世界末端 , 在一個專利家和保守家庭 。
no wonder that by age five i was a raging feminist although the term had not reached chile yet , so nobody knew what the heck was wrong with me .	不管是五歲的女性主義者 , 雖然沒有人接觸到黑猩猩 , 所以沒有人知道他對我說什麼是錯的 。
i would soon find out that there was a high price to pay for my freedom , and for questioning the patriarchy .	我很快就會發現 , 有一個高價的價格來支付我的自由 , 來問我的自由 。
but i was happy to pay it , because for every blow that i received , i was able to deliver two .	但我很高興能付錢 , 因為對每個盲目 , 我可以把兩倍 。
once , when my daughter paula was in her twenties , she said to me that feminism was dated , that i should move on .	一旦我的女兒在她二十歲時 , 她跟我說我說 , 女性主義被告知 , 我應該搬進去 。
we had a memorable fight . feminism is dated ?	我們有一個可怕的戰鬥 , 女性主義被損害嗎 ?
yes , for privileged women like my daughter and all of us here today , but not for most of our sisters in the rest of the world who are still forced into premature marriage , prostitution , forced labor they have children that they don't want or they cannot feed .	是的 , 對女兒來說 , 今天我們所有人都在這裡 , 但不是我們大部分的姊妹 , 而是迫使世界上大部分的抗議 , 強迫勞勞工 , 迫勞動勞動力 , 他們有孩子們不想或他們無法餵養 。
they have no control over their bodies or their lives .	他們沒有控制他們的身體或他們的生命 。
they have no education and no freedom .	他們沒有教育和自由 。
they are raped , beaten up and sometimes killed with impunity .	他們被強暴了 , 有時候被強暴 , 有時會殺死 。
for most western young women of today , being called a feminist is an insult .	對現今大部分的西方女性來說 , 被稱為女性主義者 。
feminism has never been sexy , but let me assure you that it never stopped me from flirting , and i have seldom suffered from lack of men .	女性主義從來沒有性戀 , 但讓我保證你永遠不會阻止我從衝突中偷走我 。
feminism is not dead , by no means .	女性主義不是死 , 而是沒有意義 。
it has evolved . if you don't like the term , change it , for goddess' sake .	它已經演化了 , 如果你不喜歡詞 , 改變它 , 上帝的神秘 。
call it aphrodite , or venus , or bimbo , or whatever you want ; the name doesn't matter , as long as we understand what it is about , and we support it .	稱它為 「 英雄 」 或 「 樂觀 」 或 「 不論你想要什麼 」 的名字並不重要 , 我們支持它 。
so here's another tale of passion , and this is a sad one .	這是另一個熱情的熱情 , 這是個悲傷 。
the place is a small women's clinic in a village in bangladesh .	那個地方是一個小女性診所的診所 。
the year is 2005 .	今年是2005年 。
jenny is a young american dental hygienist who has gone to the clinic as a volunteer during her threeweek vacation .	珍妮是一位年輕的美國人 , 她已經去診斷診斷診所當的志願者 。
she's prepared to clean teeth , but when she gets there , she finds out that there are no doctors , no dentists , and the clinic is just a hut full of flies .	她準備好乾淨的牙齒 , 但當她到那裡 , 她發現沒有醫生 , 沒有醫生 , 沒有醫生 , 沒有醫生 , 而診所只是一群旗幟 。
outside , there is a line of women who have waited several hours to be treated .	外面有一系列的女性 , 等待數小時才能被治療 。
the first patient is in excruciating pain because she has several rotten molars .	第一位病人在興奮痛苦的痛因為她有數量的浪漫 。
jenny realizes that the only solution is to pull out the bad teeth .	珍妮意識到 , 唯一解決方案的解決方案 。
she's not licensed for that ; she has never done it .	她不接受這一點 ; 她從來沒有做過 。
she risks a lot and she's terrified .	她冒險很多 , 她很害怕 。
she doesn't even have the proper instruments , but fortunately she has brought some novocaine .	她甚至甚至沒有投入的建設 , 但幸運的是她沒有投票 。
jenny has a brave and passionate heart .	珍妮有勇敢和熱情心 。
she murmurs a prayer and she goes ahead with the operation .	她鼓勵一個禱告 , 她走進了一步 。
at the end , the relieved patient kisses her hands .	最後 , 改善病人的技巧 。
that day the hygienist pulls out many more teeth .	那天 , hygiener推出更多的牙齒 。
the next morning , when she comes again to the socalled clinic , her first patient is waiting for her with her husband .	隔天早上 , 當她回來時 , 她的第一位病人正在等待她的丈夫 。
the woman's face looks like a watermelon .	女人臉孔看起來像水泥一樣 。
it is so swollen that you can't even see the eyes .	你甚至看不到眼睛 。
the husband , furious , threatens to kill the american .	丈夫 , 威脅 , 威脅要殺死美國 。
jenny is horrified at what she has done , but then the translator explains that the patient's condition has nothing to do with the operation .	珍妮是她所做的 , 但後來翻譯者解釋病人的條件 , 然後翻譯者解釋病人的條件 。
the day before , her husband beat her up because she was not home in time to prepare dinner for him .	在那天之前 , 她的丈夫是她的丈夫 , 因為她沒有時間去準備晚餐 。
millions of women live like this today .	現今 , 數百萬名女性住在這樣的情況下 。
they are the poorest of the poor .	他們是窮人的最窮人 。
although women do twothirds of the world's labor , they own less than one percent of the world's assets .	雖然世界實驗室做了兩分之二的勞工 , 他們擁有不到1%的資產 。
they are paid less than men for the same work if they're paid at all , and they remain vulnerable because they have no economic independence , and they are constantly threatened by exploitation , violence and abuse .	他們比同一份工作的薪水比男性更少 , 而且他們仍然很脆弱 , 因為他們沒有經濟獨立的經濟獨立、暴力、暴力、暴力、暴力和虐待 。
it is a fact that giving women education , work , the ability to control their own income , inherit and own property , benefits the society .	這是女性教育、工作、工作、工作、工作、工作、能力控制自己的收入 , 以及社會的能力 。
if a woman is empowered , her children and her family will be better off .	如果一個女人被賦予 , 她的家人 , 她的家庭會變得更好 。
if families prosper , the village prospers , and eventually so does the whole country .	如果家庭專家 , 村莊專家 , 最終 , 整個國家都如此 。
wangari maathai goes to a village in kenya .	亞里馬馬馬馬拉走到肯亞 。
she talks with the women and explains that the land is barren because they have cut and sold the trees .	她和女人談到 , 解釋土地是障礙 , 因為他們有砍伐樹木 。
she gets the women to plant new trees and water them , drop by drop .	她把女性送到新樹木和水 , 用乾淨的飲料 。
in a matter of five or six years , they have a forest , the soil is enriched , and the village is saved .	在五到六年間 , 他們有森林 , 土壤是被逮捕 , 村落被拯救 。
the poorest and most backward societies are always those that put women down .	最貧窮的社會總是那些把女性放下來 。
yet this obvious truth is ignored by governments and also by philanthropy .	但這顯然是政府和慈善機構 。
for every dollar given to a women's program , 20 dollars are given to men's programs .	每個月都給一個女性的程式 , 20美元被賦予男性的程式 。
women are 51 percent of humankind .	女性是51%的人類皮膚 。
empowering them will change everything more than technology and design and entertainment .	賦予他們更多的科技和娛樂 。
i can promise you that women working together linked , informed and educated can bring peace and prosperity to this forsaken planet .	我可以告訴各位 , 女性一起合作 , 改造和平靜的能力 , 教育可以帶來和平靜的行星 。
in any war today , most of the casualties are civilians , mainly women and children . they are collateral damage .	在任何戰爭中 , 大部分的營養都是公民 , 主要是女性和孩子 。 他們都是同性戀損害 。
men run the world , and look at the mess we have .	男人跑遍世界 , 看看我們有的記憶 。
what kind of world do we want ?	我們想要什麼 ?
this is a fundamental question that most of us are asking .	這是個基本問題 , 我們大多數人都在問的 。
does it make sense to participate in the existing world order ?	它是否可以參與這個世界秩序嗎 ?
we want a world where life is preserved and the quality of life is enriched for everybody , not only for the privileged .	我們希望一個生活在哪裡 , 生命的品質是讓人感到驚訝 , 而不只是為了私人的私人 。
in january i saw an exhibit of fernando botero's paintings at the uc berkeley library .	在日本 , 我看到一位法國博士的畫面 , 在核柏克萊圖書館裡 ,
no museum or gallery in the united states , except for the new york gallery that carries botero's work , has dared to show the paintings because the theme is the abu ghraib prison .	美國的博物館或gallerylery的概念 , 為紐約galles的作品 , 爸爸爸爸是為了展示畫畫畫畫的 , 因為味道是個ghraibrion監獄 。
they are huge paintings of torture and abuse of power , in the voluminous botero style .	他們很大的畫面和虐待的力量 , 在極大的底層 。
i have not been able to get those images out of my mind or my heart .	我沒有辦法把這些影像從我的心裡或我的心臟 。
what i fear most is power with impunity .	我最害怕的是不可能的力量 。
i fear abuse of power , and the power to abuse .	我害怕權力的虐待 。
in our species , the alpha males define reality , and force the rest of the pack to accept that reality and follow the rules .	在我們的物種中 , 雄性雄性定義現實 , 而其它其他規則 , 遵循現實和遵循規則 。
the rules change all the time , but they always benefit them , and in this case , the trickledown effect , which does not work in economics , works perfectly .	規則每次都改變 , 但他們總是有益益處 , 在這個案例中 , 難以置信的效應 , 這並不適合 。
abuse trickles down from the top of the ladder to the bottom .	從女士的頂端 , 從女士到下面 。
women and children , especially the poor , are at the bottom .	女人和孩子 , 尤其是窮人 , 尤其是在底下 。
even the most destitute of men have someone they can abuse a woman or a child .	即使大多數男人都有可以虐待女性或小孩 。
i'm fed up with the power that a few exert over the many through gender , income , race , and class .	我與許多性別的力量 , 在許多性別中 , 收入許多性別、收入、階級、課堂 。
i think that the time is ripe to make fundamental changes in our civilization .	我認為 , 時間是要創造基礎的改變 。
but for real change , we need feminine energy in the management of the world .	但為了真實改變世界 , 我們需要女性的管理 。
we need a critical number of women in positions of power , and we need to nurture the feminine energy in men .	我們需要一個關鍵數字的女性數量 , 而我們需要監控男性的位置 。
i'm talking about men with young minds , of course .	我在談論年輕思想的男人當然 。
old guys are hopeless ; we have to wait for them to die off .	老人是無希望 ; 我們必須等待他們死去 。
yes , i would love to have sophia loren's long legs and legendary breasts .	是的 , 我很愛去有物理和法律偏見 。
but given a choice , i would rather have the warrior hearts of wangari maathai , somaly mam , jenny and rose mapendo .	但給了一個選擇 , 我不想有戰爭的心臟心臟 , 所以馬上 , 非常哺乳類、珍妮和羅馬的地圖 。
i want to make this world good .	我想讓這個世界很好 。
not better , but to make it good .	更好 , 但要讓它變得好 。
why not ? it is possible . look around in this room all this knowledge , energy , talent and technology .	為什麼不 ? 它可以在這個房間裡看看這個知識、能源、能源、技術 。
let's get off our fannies , roll up our sleeves and get to work , passionately , in creating an almost perfect world .	咱們來看看我們的法國 , 把我們的選舉起來 , 熱情地 , 創造了一個幾乎完美的世界 。
every day , in a city the size of london , 30 million meals are served . but where does all the food come from ? architect carolyn steel discusses the daily miracle of feeding a city , and shows how ancient food routes shaped the modern world .	每天 , 在倫敦的城市大小 , 有300萬個財富都在哪裡 ? 建築師們都在哪裡 ? 建築師們每天都在飛行城市裡 , 看看古老的食物路徑 。
cities , culture , food , global issues	城市、文化、食物、食物、全球議題 。
carolyn steel: how food shapes our cities	卡羅•史蒂芬:食物塑造我們的城市如何塑造我們的城市 。
how do you feed a city ?	你要如何餵飽一個城市 ?
it's one of the great questions of our time .	這是我們的時間最棒的問題之一 。
yet it's one that's rarely asked .	但這是一個很少被問過的 。
we take it for granted that if we go into a shop or restaurant , or indeed into this theater's foyer in about an hour's time , there is going to be food there waiting for us , having magically come from somewhere .	我們把它帶到店裡 , 如果我們進入一間店或餐廳裡 , 或是在這個劇院裡 , 我們將會有很大的食物 , 等待我們 , 在那裡等待我們 , 有魔術地從某個地方開始 。
but when you think that every day for a city the size of london , enough food has to be produced , transported , bought and sold , cooked , eaten , disposed of , and that something similar has to happen every day for every city on earth , it's remarkable that cities get fed at all .	但當你認為在倫敦的城市大小食物的大小食物必須生產、運輸、交通、吃、吃、吃、吃、吃、吃、吃、吃、吃、吃、吃、吃、食物 , 都不可思議的城市 。
we live in places like this as if they're the most natural things in the world , forgetting that because we're animals and that we need to eat , we're actually as dependent on the natural world as our ancient ancestors were .	我們住在世界中最自然的事情 , 如他們是世界上最自然的事情 , 因為我們是動物的 , 我們需要吃 , 我們其實是當祖先的祖先 。
and as more of us move into cities , more of that natural world is being transformed into extraordinary landscapes like the one behind me it's soybean fields in mato grosso in brazil in order to feed us .	隨著我們移動到城市中 , 更多自然的世界越來越多的景象 , 像我在巴西的土地景中 , 像我一樣在巴西 , 為了餵飽我們 。
these are extraordinary landscapes , but few of us ever get to see them .	這些是不凡的景景象 , 但有些人有些人可能看到他們 。
and increasingly these landscapes are not just feeding us either .	令人驚訝的是這些土地景不只是餵食使用者 。
as more of us move into cities , more of us are eating meat , so that a third of the annual grain crop globally now gets fed to animals rather than to us human animals .	隨著我們移動到城市裡 , 更多使用肉肉肉肉類的三分之一 , 現在全球的三分之一 , 而不是人類動物 。
and given that it takes three times as much grain actually ten times as much grain to feed a human if it's passed through an animal first , that's not a very efficient way of feeding us .	儘管它花了三倍的時間 , 如果它通過動物第一次餵飽人類 , 那不是很有效率的方式來餵飽我們 。
and it's an escalating problem too .	這也是個計算問題 。
by 2050 , it's estimated that twice the number of us are going to be living in cities .	到了2050年 , 估計我們將會住在城市裡 。
and it's also estimated that there is going to be twice as much meat and dairy consumed .	它也估計 , 估計要多達兩倍的脂肪和髮型消費 。
so meat and urbanism are rising hand in hand .	所以 , 脂肪和城市主義正在擴張手裡 。
and that's going to pose an enormous problem .	這將會是很大的問題 。
six billion hungry carnivores to feed , by 2050 .	六十億名飢餓卡尼革命 , 到2050年 。
that's a big problem . and actually if we carry on as we are , it's a problem we're very unlikely to be able to solve .	這是個大問題 , 如果我們在於我們身上 , 它是個問題 , 我們很不太可能解決的問題 。
nineteen million hectares of rainforest are lost every year to create new arable land .	九十億英畝的雨林都失去了雨林 。
although at the same time we're losing an equivalent amount of existing arables to salinization and erosion .	雖然同時 , 我們也失去了一大堆存在的永續化和商業化 。
we're very hungry for fossil fuels too .	我們對石油燃料燃料燃料 。
it takes about 10 calories to produce every calorie of food that we consume in the west .	我們花了大約10個卡路里來製造每公公里的食物 。
and even though there is food that we are producing at great cost , we don't actually value it .	儘管有很大的成本 , 我們沒有真正價值 。
half the food produced in the usa is currently thrown away .	美國有一半食物生產的一半食物生產 。
and to end all of this , at the end of this long process , we're not even managing to feed the planet properly .	至於這個長期過程結束 , 我們甚至甚至不用用用飛行星來餵飽地球 。
a billion of us are obese , while a further billion starve .	數十億人是肥胖的 , 雖然有十億顆星 。
none of it makes very much sense .	沒有它會變得非常合理 。
and when you think that 80 percent of global trade in food now is controlled by just five multinational corporations , it's a grim picture .	當你認為 , 在食物中80%的全球貿易公司被控制了 , 只有五種不同的胰島素 。
as we're moving into cities , the world is also embracing a western diet .	當我們搬進城市裡 , 世界也在擁抱一個西方飲食 。
and if we look to the future , it's an unsustainable diet .	如果我們看看未來 , 它是個不確定的飲食 。
so how did we get here ?	所以 , 我們要如何得到這個呢 ?
and more importantly , what are we going to do about it ?	更重要的是 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
well , to answer the slightly easier question first , about 10 , 000 years ago , i would say , is the beginning of this process in the ancient near east , known as the fertile crescent .	為了回答第一 , 要回答一萬年前 , 我會說 , 大約有10萬年前 , 我會說 , 身為fert檔案的開端 。
because , as you can see , it was crescent shaped .	因為 , 如你所見 , 這是最近的形狀 。
and it was also fertile .	這也是很棒的 。
and it was here , about 10 , 000 years ago , that two extraordinary inventions , agriculture and urbanism , happened roughly in the same place and at the same time .	這裡有大約10萬年前 , 農業和城市主義 , 農業和城市主義一樣 , 農業和城市主義一樣 。
this is no accident , because agriculture and cities are bound together . they need each other .	這不是意外 , 因為農業和城市都在互相連結在一起 。 他們需要彼此 。
because it was discovery of grain by our ancient ancestors for the first time that produced a food source that was large enough and stable enough to support permanent settlements .	因為這是我們的古老祖先的發現 , 生產出一種食物源源頭 , 可以支撐永久的食物源源源頭 。
and if we look at what those settlements were like , we see they were compact .	如果我們看看這些設備是什麼樣子 。
they were surrounded by productive farm land and dominated by large temple complexes like this one at ur , that were , in fact , effectively , spiritualized , central food distribution centers .	他們被生產力的農場 , 由大型的溫度 , 由大型的溫度 , 就像這樣 , 特別是 , 精神化療中心的食物分佈中心 。
because it was the temples that organized the harvest , gathered in the grain , offered it to the gods , and then offered the grain that the gods didn't eat back to the people .	因為它是廢棄物的溫度 , 將它帶到上帝 , 把它放在上帝 , 然後提供給上帝 , 然後提供給上帝的人 。
so , if you like , the whole spiritual and physical life of these cities was dominated by the grain and the harvest that sustained them .	所以 , 如果你喜歡 , 整個城市的精神和實體生活生活生活的一部分 , 由穀物和棲息相關 。
and in fact , that's true of every ancient city .	事實上 , 這是每個古老城市的真實城市 。
but of course not all of them were that small .	但當然不是所有人都這樣 。
famously , rome had about a million citizens by the first century a . d .	很有名 , 羅馬有大約一百萬名公民 。
so how did a city like this feed itself ?	那麼這個城市是怎麼樣的 ?
the answer is what i call " ancient food miles . "	答案是 , 我稱之為 「 古老食物 」
basically , rome had access to the sea , which made it possible for it to import food from a very long way away .	基本上 , 羅馬必須取得海域 , 讓它從一個非常長遠的食物 。
this is the only way it was possible to do this in the ancient world , because it was very difficult to transport food over roads , which were rough .	這是科學世界唯一能做到的唯一方法 , 因為它非常困難 , 因為它很難運送食物跨路路路路路徑 , 非常困難 。
and the food obviously went off very quickly .	食物顯然的食物很快 。
so rome effectively waged war on places like carthage and egypt just to get its paws on their grain reserves .	所以 , 羅馬有效地勇氣和埃及的埃及只能把它放在他們的穀物上 。
and , in fact , you could say that the expansion of the empire was really sort of one long , drawn out militarized shopping spree , really .	事實上 , 你可以說 , 帝國的擴張是很長、很長、很長的軍事購物速度 , 真的 。
in fact i love the fact , i just have to mention this: rome in fact used to import oysters from london , at one stage . i think that's extraordinary .	事實上 , 我愛事實是 , 我必須提到這一點:羅馬的角色從倫敦到倫敦 , 在一個階段中 , 我想這是很不凡的 。
so rome shaped its hinterland through its appetite .	所以羅馬的形狀 , 羅馬的形狀 。
but the interesting thing is that the other thing also happened in the preindustrial world .	但有趣的是 , 最初發生在普通世界中發生的事 。
if we look at a map of london in the 17th century , we can see that its grain , which is coming in from the thames , along the bottom of this map .	如果我們看看十七世紀的倫敦地圖 , 我們可以看到它的穀物 , 來自這個地圖的底部 , 沿著這個地圖的底部 。
so the grain markets were to the south of the city .	所以 , 穀物市場是到城市的南部 。
and the roads leading up from them to cheapside , which was the main market , were also grain markets .	路徑從他們到便宜的路徑 , 這是主要市場 , 主要市場也包含市場 。
and if you look at the name of one of those streets , bread street , you can tell what was going on there 300 years ago .	如果你看看那些街道的名字 , 街道的名字 , 你可以告訴你在300年前發生了什麼事 。
and the same of course was true for fish .	當然 , 魚也同樣是魚類的 。
fish was , of course , coming in by river as well . same thing .	當然 , 魚當然 , 透過河流來 。
and of course billingsgate , famously , was london's fish market , operating onsite here until the mid1980s .	當然 , 野生市場 , 很有名 , 是倫敦的魚市場 , 直到1980年代 , 直到1980年代 。
which is extraordinary , really , when you think about it .	這是很不凡的 , 當你想到它的時候 。
everybody else was wandering around with mobile phones that looked like bricks and sort of smelly fish happening down on the port .	其他人都在用手機上 , 看起來像布里克 , 看起來像布里克和類似的魚類 。
this is another thing about food in cities: once its roots into the city are established , they very rarely move .	這是城市裡的另一件事:一旦它根根根根植入城市中 , 它們非常快地移動 。
meat is a very different story because , of course , animals could walk into the city .	脂肪是一種非常不同的故事 , 因為動物可以走進城市裡 。
so much of london's meat was coming from the northwest , from scotland and wales .	倫敦的大部份來自北部、蘇格蘭和沃爾 。
so it was coming in , and arriving at the city at the northwest , which is why smithfield , london's very famous meat market , was located up there .	所以 , 北部在北部最北部 , 這就是為什麼mitheld、倫敦非常有名的肉品市場 , 倫敦很有名 。
poultry was coming in from east anglia and so on , to the northeast .	詩人從東亞開始 , 到北部 , 到北岸 。
i feel a bit like a weather woman doing this . anyway , and so the birds were coming in with their feet protected with little canvas shoes .	我覺得有點像aththther女人在做這件事 , 所以鳥類在牠們腳上 , 牠的鳥類 。
and then when they hit the eastern end of cheapside , that's where they were sold , which is why it's called poultry .	然後當他們撞擊東岸結束時 , 這就是為什麼他們被賣出來的原因 , 這就是為什麼它稱作 「 詩人 」 。
and , in fact , if you look at the map of any city built before the industrial age , you can trace food coming in to it .	事實上 , 如果你看看任何城市的地圖 , 你可以在工業時代之前建立的食物 。
you can actually see how it was physically shaped by food , both by reading the names of the streets , which give you a lot of clues .	你可以看到它是如何由食物的名字 , 透過閱讀街道的名字 , 給你很多clus 。
friday street , in a previous life , is where you went to buy your fish on a friday .	星期五街上 , 在一個星期五街上 , 你去買你的魚魚 。
but also you have to imagine it full of food .	但 , 你必須想像它全部食物 。
because the streets and the public spaces were the only places where food was bought and sold .	因為街道和公共空間的唯一地方是食物被買到的唯一地方 。
and if we look at an image of smithfield in 1830 you can see that it would have been very difficult to live in a city like this and be unaware of where your food came from .	如果我們看看1830年 , 你可以看到 , 它會非常困難 , 就像這個城市一樣很難住在像這樣的城市裡 , 你的食物來自哪裡 , 你的食物來自哪裡 。
in fact , if you were having sunday lunch , the chances were it was mooing or bleating outside your window about three days earlier .	事實上 , 如果你有星期日午餐午餐 , 機會在你的窗戶外 , 可能在你的窗戶外外 , 大約三天早上 。
so this was obviously an organic city , part of an organic cycle .	這很顯然是一個機械城市的一部分 。
and then 10 years later everything changed .	十年後 , 一切都改變了 。
this is an image of the great western in 1840 .	這是1840年代最偉大的西方人 。
and as you can see , some of the earliest train passengers were pigs and sheep .	如你所見 , 有些最早的訓練乘客是豬豬 , 牠的豬 。
so all of a sudden , these animals are no longer walking into market .	所以突然間 , 這些動物不再走進市場 。
they're being slaughtered out of sight and mind , somewhere in the countryside .	他們被拒絕了 , 心中 , 有些地方在援助中 。
and they're coming into the city by rail .	他們會進入城市的城市 。
and this changes everything .	這改變一切 。
to start off with , it makes it possible for the first time to grow cities , really any size and shape , in any place .	首先 , 它讓它成長城市變得有可能 , 任何大小、形狀、形狀、形狀、任何地方 。
cities used to be constrained by geography ; they used to have to get their food through very difficult physical means .	城市常常常被地理混合在一起 , 他們以前必須透過非常困難的實體意義 。
all of a sudden they are effectively emancipated from geography .	突然間 , 他們很有效地從geographyography 。
and as you can see from these maps of london , in the 90 years after the trains came , it goes from being a little blob that was quite easy to feed by animals coming in on foot , and so on , to a large splurge , that would be very , very difficult to feed with anybody on foot , either animals or people .	如你所看到的這些地圖 , 在90年之後 , 火車從一小塊小塊開始 , 它從一隻小鳥飛到腳上 , 所以 , 到一隻大型的脊椎動物 , 很難餵飽任何人 , 牠們很難餵飽任何人 。
and of course that was just the beginning . after the trains came cars , and really this marks the end of this process .	當然那只是一開始 。 在火車之後 , 火車結束後 , 真的是這個過程的 。
it's the final emancipation of the city from any apparent relationship with nature at all .	這是金融胚胎的城市 , 從任何顯然的關係 。
and this is the kind of city that's devoid of smell , devoid of mess , certainly devoid of people , because nobody would have dreamed of walking in such a landscape .	這是嗅覺的城市 , 避免嗅覺的城市 , 可能避免人們 , 因為沒有人會在這樣的土地景中 , 因為沒有人會夢想走進這樣的景象 。
in fact , what they did to get food was they got in their cars , drove to a box somewhere on the outskirts , came back with a week's worth of shopping , and wondered what on earth to do with it .	事實上 , 他們要得到食物是他們車子裡的食物 , 喝到一盒盒盒子裡 , 回來了一週購物 , 回到地球上 。
and this really is the moment when our relationship , both with food and cities , changes completely .	這真的是當我們的關係時 , 兩者都完全改變了 。
here we have food that used to be the center , the social core of the city at the periphery .	我們有食物 , 以前我們有食物的社會核心社會核心 。
it used to be a social event , buying and selling food .	以前它曾經是社交活動 , 購買食物 。
we used to cook ; now we just add water , or a little bit of an egg if you're making a cake or something .	我們以前都得烹飪 , 或有點蛋白質 , 如果你在製造一隻貓或東西 。
we don't smell food to see if it's okay to eat .	我們不聞聞聞 , 看看它是否好吃 。
we just read the back of a label on a packet .	我們剛剛讀過一個實驗室的實驗室 。
and we don't value food . we don't trust it .	我們沒有價值食物 。 我們不相信它 。
so instead of trusting it , we fear it .	所以不是信任它 , 我們害怕它 。
and instead of valuing it , we throw it away .	而不是評估它 , 而是把它丟掉 。
one of the great ironies of modern food systems is that they've made the very thing they promised to make easier much harder .	現代食物系統之一是他們所承諾的最偉大的諷刺之一是他們承諾的 。
by making it possible to build cities anywhere and any place , they've actually distanced us from our most important relationship , which is that of us and nature .	藉由讓城市建造城市的任何地方 , 他們真的距離我們最重要的關係 , 就是我們和自然之間的距離 。
and also they've made us dependent on systems that only they can deliver , that , as we've seen , are unsustainable .	而且他們也讓我們依賴系統的獨立系統 , 只要我們看過 , 那就算我們看過 , 沒有永續性 。
so what are we going to do about that ?	那麼 , 我們要怎麼做 ?
it's not a new question .	這不是新的問題 。
500 years ago it's what thomas more was asking himself .	500年前 , 它就是問自己自己自己自己自己 。
this is the frontispiece of his book " utopia . "	這是他的《烏托邦》 。
and it was a series of semiindependent citystates , if that sounds remotely familiar , a day's walk from one another where everyone was basically farmingmad , and grew vegetables in their back gardens , and ate communal meals together , and so on .	這是一系列的一系列城市 , 如果這聽起來很熟悉的城市 , 如果聽起來聽起來很熟悉 , 每天都從另一邊的農場 , 每個人基本上都是農業的農場 。
and i think you could argue that food is a fundamental ordering principle of utopia , even though more never framed it that way .	我認為你可以說食物是基礎的基本元素 , 即使比亞的原則 , 甚至從來沒有框架 。
and here is another very famous " utopian " vision , that of ebenezer howard , " the garden city . "	這是另一個非常有名的 「 烏托邦 」 的願景 , 這位埃及城市 。
same idea: series of semiindependent citystates , little blobs of metropolitan stuff with arable land around , joined to one another by railway .	同樣的點子:一系列各式各樣的城市 , 小小塊塊塊塊塊塊塊塊塊 , 加入到另一端 , 加入另一端 , 加入另一端 。
and again , food could be said to be the ordering principle of his vision .	再一次 , 食物可以跟他談的原則 。
it even got built , but nothing to do with this vision that howard had .	甚至是建造的 , 但沒有東西去做這個觀點 。
and that is the problem with these utopian ideas , that they are utopian .	這就是這些烏托邦思想的問題 , 他們是美麗的 。
utopia was actually a word that thomas moore used deliberately .	烏托邦其實是個詞彙 ,
it was a kind of joke , because it's got a double derivation from the greek .	這是個笑話 , 因為它有一個懷疑 , 來自希臘的現代活動 。
it can either mean a good place , or no place .	它可以說是好的地方 , 或是沒有地方的地方 。
because it's an ideal . it's an imaginary thing . we can't have it .	因為這是一個想法 , 它是一種想像力 , 我們不能擁有它 。

karen armstrong: let's revive the golden rule	karen軍隊:咱們來拯救黃金規則 。
for years i've been feeling frustrated , because as a religious historian , i've become acutely aware of the centrality of compassion in all the major world faiths .	幾年來 , 我感到挫折 , 因為身為宗教的歷史學家 , 我已經成為了一個非常有意識的同情心 。
every single one of them has evolved their own version of what's been called the golden rule .	每一個人都有進化自己的版本都演化了他們的版本 。
sometimes it comes in a positive version " always treat all others as you'd like to be treated yourself . "	有時候它會出現在一個正面的版本中 , 你想要被治療自己 。 」
and equally important is the negative version " don't do to others what you would not like them to do to you . "	同樣重要的是 , 負面版本 " 不要跟別人做的事 。 "
look into your own heart , discover what it is that gives you pain and then refuse , under any circumstance whatsoever , to inflict that pain on anybody else .	看看你的心臟 , 發現它是什麼讓你痛苦 , 然後拒絕任何情況 , 在任何人身上的情況下 , 在任何人身上 。
and people have emphasized the importance of compassion , not just because it sounds good , but because it works .	人們有同情心的重要性 , 不僅是因為它聽起來很棒 , 但是因為它是運作的 。
people have found that when they have implemented the golden rule as confucius said , " all day and every day , " not just a question of doing your good deed for the day and then returning to a life of greed and egotism , but to do it all day and every day , you dethrone yourself from the center of your world , put another there , and you transcend yourself .	人們發現 , 當他們被改善黃金規則時 , 每天都會說: 「 每天和你一起做好準備好 , 不僅僅是做好好的決定 , 每一天 , 你都要從你的世界中心的中心 , 你將自己轉換為你世界的中心 。
and it brings you into the presence of what's been called god , nirvana , rama , tao .	然後它帶你進了什麼樣子 , nira、rama、o、oma、o、o 。
something that goes beyond what we know in our egobound existence .	我們所知道的東西在我們的演算法中所知的事物 。
but you know you'd never know it a lot of the time , that this was so central to the religious life .	但你知道你永遠不知道 , 很多時候這是宗教生活的中心 。
because with a few wonderful exceptions , very often when religious people come together , religious leaders come together , they're arguing about abstruse doctrines or uttering a council of hatred or inveighing against homosexuality or something of that sort .	因為有一些很棒的昂貴 , 通常當宗教領袖聚在一起時 , 宗教領袖聚在一起時 , 他們正在爭取的宗教領袖 , 他們正在爭取的仇恨或打破仇恨或被迫害的行為 。
often people don't really want to be compassionate .	通常人們不喜歡同情心 。

and that of course defeats the object of the exercise .	當然這當然是沙漠的物體 。

if we don't manage to implement the golden rule globally , so that we treat all peoples , wherever and whoever they may be , as though they were as important as ourselves , i doubt that we'll have a viable world to hand on to the next generation .	如果我們不能夠改善全球規則全球規則 , 所以我們治療所有人 , 無論他們在哪裡 , 無論他們是很重要的 , 雖然他們對下一代來說 , 我會懷疑下一個世代的世界 。
the task of our time , one of the great tasks of our time , is to build a global society , as i said , where people can live together in peace .	在我們的時間中 , 其中一個偉大任務之一 , 就是建立一個全球社會社會 , 如我所說的 , 人們能一起住在和平 。

thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
mit researcher skylar tibbits works on selfassembly the idea that instead of building something , we can create materials that build themselves , much the way a strand of dna zips itself together . it's a big concept at early stages ; tibbits shows us three inthelab projects that hint at what a selfassembling future might look like .	麻省理工學院研究員在自我組合的概念 , 而不是建築物 , 我們能創造自己自己 , 我們可以創造自己的材料 , 很多方法 , 我們可以創造自己 , 更大的概念 , 它是一個很大的概念 , 抗拒我們三個在初期期階段中 , 抗拒我們三倍的未來 。
skylar tibbits: can we make things that make themselves ?	天空抗議:我們可以讓自己做出自己自己做的事嗎 ?
today i'd like to show you the future of the way we make things .	今天我要向各位展示我們製作的東西 。
i believe that soon our buildings and machines will be selfassembling , replicating and repairing themselves .	我相信 , 我們的建築和機器會自我組合、複製、複製、複製和複製自己 。
so i'm going to show you what i believe is the current state of manufacturing , and then compare that to some natural systems .	所以我要給各位看我相信的是製造製造製造的狀態 , 然後把這些自然系統放在某些自然系統中 。
so in the current state of manufacturing , we have skyscrapers two and a half years [of assembly time] , 500 , 000 to a million parts , fairly complex , new , exciting technologies in steel , concrete , glass .	所以在製造製造過程中 , 我們有天空工匠兩到半年半 , 大約有500萬個部分 , 很複雜 , 非常複雜 , 令人興奮 , 很興奮 , 魅惑的技術 , 魅惑、玻璃 。
we have exciting machines that can take us into space five years [of assembly time] , 2 . 5 million parts .	我們很興奮的機器可以帶我們到太空中 , 2.5千萬個部分 。
but on the other side , if you look at the natural systems , we have proteins that have two million types , can fold in 10 , 000 nanoseconds , or dna with three billion base pairs we can replicate in roughly an hour .	但另一方面 , 如果你看看自然系統 , 我們有蛋白質系統 , 我們有兩百萬種種類 , 可以在一小時內摺疊 , 或dna , dna有3億個鹼基組成 。
so there's all of this complexity in our natural systems , but they're extremely efficient , far more efficient than anything we can build , far more complex than anything we can build .	所以 , 在我們的自然系統中 , 有許多複雜性 , 但他們非常有效率 , 比我們所能建造的更複雜 , 比我們所能建造的更複雜 。
they're far more efficient in terms of energy .	他們比能源更有效率 。
they hardly ever make mistakes .	他們幾乎不可能犯錯 。
and they can repair themselves for longevity .	他們可以重複自己長久以來 。
so there's something super interesting about natural systems .	所以有趣關於自然系統系統 。
and if we can translate that into our built environment , then there's some exciting potential for the way that we build things .	如果我們能把這個建築轉變成我們的環境 , 那麼有一些令人興奮的潛力 。
and i think the key to that is selfassembly .	我認為關鍵是自我組合 。
so if we want to utilize selfassembly in our physical environment , i think there's four key factors .	所以如果我們想要把自我組成自我組合 , 我認為有四個關鍵因素 。
the first is that we need to decode all of the complexity of what we want to build so our buildings and machines .	首先 , 我們需要確保所有我們想要建造的所有複雜性和機器 。
and we need to decode that into simple sequences basically the dna of how our buildings work .	我們需要確保這個簡單的序列基本上是如何運作的dna 。
then we need programmable parts that can take that sequence and use that to fold up , or reconfigure .	接著 , 我們需要程式可以把這些序列放起來 , 用它來摺疊 , 或重建 。
we need some energy that's going to allow that to activate , allow our parts to be able to fold up from the program .	我們需要一些能量 , 使我們的部分能夠激動我們的部分 , 允許我們從計畫中得到的能量 。
and we need some type of error correction redundancy to guarantee that we have successfully built what we want .	我們需要一些類型的錯誤 , 來保證我們有成功地建立我們想要的 。
so i'm going to show you a number of projects that my colleagues and i at mit are working on to achieve this selfassembling future .	所以我要給你們看一些我的同事 , 我在麻省理工學院工作 , 我在麻省理工的未來 。
the first two are the macrobot and decibot .	首先 , 第一兩個是雄性和決定 。
so these projects are largescale reconfigurable robots 8 ft . , 12 ft . long proteins .	所以這些計畫是大規模的機器人 , 12英尺 , 12英尺 , 12英尺長的蛋白質 。
they're embedded with mechanical electrical devices , sensors .	他們與機械裝置機械裝置、感應器 。
you decode what you want to fold up into , into a sequence of angles so negative 120 , negative 120 , 0 , 0 , 120 , negative 120 something like that ; so a sequence of angles , or turns , and you send that sequence through the string .	你知道你想要摺疊的東西 , 進入一個角度的120 , 000 , 負面120 , 000 , 負面120 , 000 , 負面120 , 負面120、1、120、1、120、負面的序列 。
each unit takes its message so negative 120 it rotates to that , checks if it got there and then passes it to its neighbor .	每個單位都拿它訊息給負面120倍 , 看看它 , 然後把它傳送到鄰居 。
so these are the brilliant scientists , engineers , designers that worked on this project .	這些是偉大科學家、工程師、工程師、工程師、設計師、設計師 ,
and i think it really brings to light: is this really scalable ?	我認為這真的帶給光:這真的很可怕嗎 ?
i mean , thousands of dollars , lots of man hours made to make this eightfoot robot .	我的意思是 , 數千美元 , 許多人花了這八英尺機器人 。
can we really scale this up ? can we really embed robotics into every part ?	我們能否否否把機器人放到每一部分 ? 我們真的能把機器人放到每一個部分嗎 ?
the next one questions that and looks at passive nature , or passively trying to have reconfiguration programmability .	下一個問題 , 看看熱情的自然 , 或是活著著的規劃計畫 。
but it goes a step further , and it tries to have actual computation .	但它會變得更進一步 , 它試圖有實際計算計算 。
it basically embeds the most fundamental building block of computing , the digital logic gate , directly into your parts .	它基本上被組成最基本的建築物 , 數位化合物的數位建築物 , 直接進入你的部分 。
so this is a nand gate .	這是個nandgateates 。
you have one tetrahedron which is the gate that's going to do your computing , and you have two input tetrahedrons .	你有一顆廢棄物 , 就是要做你的計算 , 你有兩個輸入 。
one of them is the input from the user , as you're building your bricks .	其中之一是來自使用者的輸入 , 如你建造你的麵包 。
the other one is from the previous brick that was placed .	另一種是來自前前前往的 。
and then it gives you an output in 3d space .	然後它給你一個3d空間 。
so what this means is that the user can start plugging in what they want the bricks to do .	所以這意味著 , 使用者可以開始在他們想要做的事 。
it computes on what it was doing before and what you said you wanted it to do .	它計算在它之前所做的 , 然後你說你想要做的事 。
and now it starts moving in threedimensional space so up or down .	現在它開始在三維空間中移動到三維空間 。
so on the lefthand side , [1 , 1] input equals 0 output , which goes down .	所以左撇子左撇子 , 1.1.1.1.1.
on the righthand side , [0 , 0] input is a 1 output , which goes up .	在右手邊 , 0 , 輸入是1個輸出的 。
and so what that really means is that our structures now contain the blueprints of what we want to build .	所以這意味著我們的結構現在已經存在於我們想要建造的藍圖印 。
so they have all of the information embedded in them of what was constructed .	所以他們有所有的資訊都被組成了 。
so that means that we can have some form of selfreplication .	也就是說 , 我們可以有一些自我移植 。
in this case i call it selfguided replication , because your structure contains the exact blueprints .	在這個例子中 , 我稱它為自我懷疑 , 因為你的結構保持藍圖 。
if you have errors , you can replace a part .	如果你有更糟糕 , 你可以複製一部分 。
all the local information is embedded to tell you how to fix it .	所有地方資訊都被賦予你如何解決它 。
so you could have something that climbs along and reads it and can output at one to one .	所以你可以在一個爬上 , 閱讀它 , 讀它 , 可以在一個人身上 。
it's directly embedded ; there's no external instructions .	直接擁抱了 ; 沒有外交機構 。
so the last project i'll show is called biased chains , and it's probably the most exciting example that we have right now of passive selfassembly systems .	所以最後一個計畫叫做偏見鏈鏈 , 它可能是最令人興奮的例子 , 我們現在現在有活躍的自我組合系統 。
so it takes the reconfigurability and programmability and makes it a completely passive system .	所以 , 它將重建和程式的能力 , 讓它完全活躍的系統 。
so basically you have a chain of elements .	所以基本上 , 你有一堆元素 。
each element is completely identical , and they're biased .	每個元素都完全相同 , 他們是偏見的 。
so each chain , or each element , wants to turn right or left .	所以每一個鏈鏈 , 或是每一個元素 , 想要把右邊或左邊 。
so as you assemble the chain , you're basically programming it .	所以當你把鏈結合起來 , 你基本上是程式碼 。
you're telling each unit if it should turn right or left .	你在告訴每個單位是否應該轉轉移或左邊 。
so when you shake the chain , it then folds up into any configuration that you've programmed in so in this case , a spiral , or in this case , two cubes next to each other .	所以當你羞辱時 , 它會把你放進任何咖啡廳裡 , 然後在這個例子中 , 一個奇蹟 , 或是在這個案例中 , 兩個方塊 , 或是在這個案例中 , 兩根根方 。
so you can basically program any threedimensional shape or onedimensional , twodimensional up into this chain completely passively .	所以你可以基本上設計任何三維空間形狀或受害者的形狀 , 兩度的感知 。
so what does this tell us about the future ?	所以 , 這告訴我們未來的是什麼 ?
i think that it's telling us that there's new possibilities for selfassembly , replication , repair in our physical structures , our buildings , machines .	我認為這是告訴我們 , 有新的可能性 , 有新的可能性 , 複製、複製、複製、修復、機器 。
there's new programmability in these parts .	在這些地方有新的程式 。
and from that you have new possibilities for computing .	從那裏你有新的可能性 。
we'll have spatial computing .	我們會有數量計算 。
imagine if our buildings , our bridges , machines , all of our bricks could actually compute .	想像一下 , 如果我們的橋樑、機器、機器、機器、機器 , 都可以計算 。
that's amazing parallel and distributed computing power , new design possibilities .	這很棒的悖論和分配能力 , 新的設計可能性 。
so it's exciting potential for this .	所以它很興奮的潛力 。
so i think these projects i've showed here are just a tiny step towards this future , if we implement these new technologies for a new selfassembling world .	所以我認為這些專案計畫只是個小步驟 , 如果我們提升這些新科技 , 若我們改善這些新的自我組合 。
we've been to the moon , we've mapped the continents , we've even been to the deepest point in the ocean twice . what's left for the next generation to explore ? biologist and explorer nathan wolfe suggests this answer: almost everything . and we can start , he says , with the world of the unseeably small .	我們一直在月球上 , 我們已經把大陸放到大陸上 , 我們甚至一直在探索海洋中最深的點點子是什麼 ? 生物學家和探索者說 , 幾乎可以開始探索這個答案:幾乎一切 。 我們能開始說 , 一切 。
biodiversity , exploration , microbiology , science	生物多樣性 , 探索、微生物學、科學、科學、科學、科學、科學、微生物多樣性 。
nathan wolfe: what's left to explore ?	nathanwolff:剩下什麼 ?
recently i visited beloit , wisconsin .	最近我訪問的信念 。

during his time at the american museum of natural history , andrews led a range of expeditions to uncharted regions , like here in the gobi desert .	在美國博物館時期 , 導致了一種自然歷史的博物館 , 讓一群被揭露出來的區域 , 就像這個目標一樣 。
he was quite a figure .	他很清楚 。
he was later , it's said , the basis of the indiana jones character .	他後來說 , 印度瓊斯說 , 印度約翰角色 。
and when i was in beloit , wisconsin , i gave a public lecture to a group of middle school students .	當我在床上的時候 , 我給了一個公共課程 , 我給一個公共學校學生 。
and i'm here to tell you , if there's anything more intimidating than talking here at ted , it'll be trying to hold the attention of a group of a thousand 12yearolds for a 45minute lecture .	我在這裡來告訴各位 , 如果有更多的受害者比ted演講的注意力 , 它會試著把一千二歲的注意力 , 它會試著把焦點放在一個45分鐘內 。
at the end of the lecture they asked a number of questions , but there was one that's really stuck with me since then .	最後他們問了一些問題 , 但這真的很困惑 , 但有一件事真的讓我感到困惑 。
there was a young girl who stood up , and she asked the question: " where should we explore ? "	有一位年輕女孩站起來 , 她問這個問題: 「 我們該探索哪裡 ? 」
i think there's a sense that many of us have that the great age of exploration on earth is over , that for the next generation they're going to have to go to outer space or the deepest oceans in order to find something significant to explore .	我認為 , 許多人都有這種探索地球上最偉大的探索 , 接下來一代他們將會去外太空或最深的海洋 , 為了尋找一些巨大的探索 。
but is that really the case ?	但這真的是這樣呢 ?
is there really nowhere significant for us to explore left here on earth ?	對我們來說 , 地球上有很大的意義嗎 ?
it sort of made me think back to one of my favorite explorers in the history of biology .	這讓我回到生物學歷史中最喜歡的探險家之一 。
this is an explorer of the unseen world , martinus beijerinck .	這是一個探索未知的世界的探索者 , 馬丁•貝丁 。
so beijerinck set out to discover the cause of tobacco mosaic disease .	所以 , 貝爾•賈斯坦克試圖發現菸草疾病的原因 。
what he did is he took the infected juice from tobacco plants and he would filter it through smaller and smaller filters .	他所做的是他把感染到菸草廠裡 , 他會透過更小、更小的濾器 。
and he reached the point where he felt that there must be something out there that was smaller than the smallest forms of life that were ever known bacteria , at the time .	他接觸到他覺得有一定比最小的東西最小的生命形式 , 比起最小的生命形式 。
he came up with a name for his mystery agent .	他來找了一名神秘的名字 。
he called it the virus latin for " poison . "	他稱它為 「 氣球 」 。
and in uncovering viruses , beijerinck really opened this entirely new world for us .	在未見過病毒、貝爾•賈斯汀真的開放了這個全新的世界 。
we now know that viruses make up the majority of the genetic information on our planet , more than the genetic information of all other forms of life combined .	現在我們知道 , 病毒在地球上大部分的基因資訊 , 比所有其他形式的基因資訊 , 比其他形式的基因信息 。
and obviously there's been tremendous practical applications associated with this world things like the eradication of smallpox , the advent of a vaccine against cervical cancer , which we now know is mostly caused by human papillomavirus .	顯然有著非常的實際應用應用程式 , 和這個世界各地各地的疫苗 , 例如疫苗所造成的疫苗 , 我們現在知道大部分是由人類武器所造成的 。
and beijerinck's discovery , this was not something that occurred 500 years ago .	在500年前發現 , 這不是發生發生發生的事 。
it was a little over 100 years ago that beijerinck discovered viruses .	這是一百年前jerinck發現病毒的病毒 。
so basically we had automobiles , but we were unaware of the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	所以基本上 , 我們有自動駕駛的生命形式 , 但我們對地球上大部分的基因資訊 。
we now have these amazing tools to allow us to explore the unseen world things like deep sequencing , which allow us to do much more than just skim the surface and look at individual genomes from a particular species , but to look at entire metagenomes , the communities of teeming microorganisms in , on and around us and to document all of the genetic information in these species .	我們現在有這些令人驚訝的工具 , 讓我們探索獨特的獨特世界 , 讓我們更能做更多的基因組 , 看看整個金屬生物原子 , 但看看整個金屬生物組的社區 , 在我們周圍的基因組中 , 在我們周圍的基因組中 。
we can apply these techniques to things from soil to skin and everything in between .	我們可以應用這些技術從土壤到皮膚和所有東西之間的一切 。
in my organization we now do this on a regular basis to identify the causes of outbreaks that are unclear exactly what causes them .	在我的組織裡 , 我們現在正在做這件事 , 來辨識出出的原因 , 不確定是什麼導致它們的原因 。
and just to give you a sense of how this works , imagine that we took a nasal swab from every single one of you .	為了給各位一個了解這個作品如何運作 , 想像一下 , 我們從每一個人身上身上得到的naala 。
and this is something we commonly do to look for respiratory viruses like influenza .	這是我們常常常做的事 , 我們常常常做的事 。
the first thing we would see is a tremendous amount of genetic information .	我們所看到的第一件事是非常大的基因資訊 。
and if we started looking into that genetic information , we'd see a number of usual suspects out there of course , a lot of human genetic information , but also bacterial and viral information , mostly from things that are completely harmless within your nose .	如果我們開始研究這個基因資訊 , 我們就會看到一些常見的假設 , 當然 , 許多人類基因資訊 , 但還有細菌和視覺資訊 , 大部分是完全無害的 。
but we'd also see something very , very surprising .	但我們也看到一些非常驚訝 。
as we started to look at this information , we would see that about 20 percent of the genetic information in your nose doesn't match anything that we've ever seen before no plant , animal , fungus , virus or bacteria .	當我們開始觀察這個資訊時 , 我們會看到大約20%的基因資訊 , 在鼻子裡 , 病毒或細菌 。
basically we have no clue what this is .	基本上 , 我們沒有確定這是什麼 。
and for the small group of us who actually study this kind of data , a few of us have actually begun to call this information biological dark matter .	對我們來說 , 對於這些數據的小群體來說 , 我們當中有些人其實都被稱為生物暗物質暗物質物質暗物質 。
we know it's not anything that we've seen before ; it's sort of the equivalent of an uncharted continent right within our own genetic information .	我們知道這不是我們以前見過的 , 它有點像是一個未知的大陸中 , 而是我們自己的基因信息 。
and there's a lot of it .	還有很多 。
if you think 20 percent of genetic information in your nose is a lot of biological dark matter , if we looked at your gut , up to 40 or 50 percent of that information is biological dark matter .	如果你認為20%的基因信息是很多生物暗物質 , 如果我們仔細觀察你的腸道 , 到40%或50%的資訊是生物暗物質暗物質暗物質 。
and even in the relatively sterile blood , around one to two percent of this information is dark matter can't be classified , can't be typed or matched with anything we've seen before .	即使在相對的血液中 , 大約有百分之二的資訊是黑暗物質 , 無法被辨識出來 , 或是我們以前見過的東西 。
at first we thought that perhaps this was artifact .	首先 , 我們認為也許這是人工智慧 。
these deep sequencing tools are relatively new .	這些深序列工具是相對的 。
but as they become more and more accurate , we've determined that this information is a form of life , or at least some of it is a form of life .	但當他們變得更加精確 , 我們已經決定這資訊是一種生命形式的形式 , 或者至少有些是生命的形式 。
and while the hypotheses for explaining the existence of biological dark matter are really only in their infancy , there's a very , very exciting possibility that exists: that buried in this life , in this genetic information , are signatures of as of yet unidentified life .	雖然假設解釋了生物暗物質的存在 , 其實只有在他們的基礎上 , 非常興奮的可能性 , 非常興奮的可能性:埋葬在這個生命中 , 在這個基因信息中 , 在這個基因信息中 , 在這個基因信息中 , 在這個基因信息中 ,
that as we explore these strings of a's , t's , c's and g's , we may uncover a completely new class of life that , like beijerinck , will fundamentally change the way that we think about the nature of biology .	當我們探索這些弦弦弦時 , t是 , 克里斯的 , 我們可能會完全完全完全改變了生物學的新課程 , 比如阿吉斯 , 基本上改變生物學的方式 。
that perhaps will allow us to identify the cause of a cancer that afflicts us or identify the source of an outbreak that we aren't familiar with or perhaps create a new tool in molecular biology .	也許可以讓我們辨識出癌症的原因 , 或是我們不熟悉的癌症因素 , 或是我們辨識出我們不熟悉的原因 。
i'm pleased to announce that , along with colleagues at stanford and caltech and ucsf , we're currently starting an initiative to explore biological dark matter for the existence of new forms of life .	我很榮幸的是 , 在史丹佛和加州大學的同事 , 我們現在現在正在開始探索生物暗物質的存在 。
a little over a hundred years ago , people were unaware of viruses , the forms of life that make up most of the genetic information on our planet .	一百年前 , 人們都不知道病毒病毒的形狀 , 讓地球上大部分的基因信息的形式 。
a hundred years from now , people may marvel that we were perhaps completely unaware of a new class of life that literally was right under our noses .	一百年來 , 人們可能結婚 , 我們可能完全無法意識到我們的鼻子裡 。
it's true , we may have charted all the continents on the planet and we may have discovered all the mammals that are out there , but that doesn't mean that there's nothing left to explore on earth .	這是真的 , 我們可能在地球上有挑戰性的所有哺乳動物 , 我們可能發現所有的哺乳動物都存在 , 但這並不意味著什麼都沒有離開地球上探索地球上 。
beijerinck and his kind provide an important lesson for the next generation of explorers people like that young girl from beloit , wisconsin .	貝爾•賈斯汀和他提供了一個很重要的課程師 , 像那些來自洛杉磯、智慧的年輕女孩 。
and i think if we phrase that lesson , it's something like this: don't assume that what we currently think is out there is the full story .	我想如果我們用這句話說 , 這有點像這樣:不要假設我們目前所認為的是完全故事 。
go after the dark matter in whatever field you choose to explore .	在任何領域中 , 不論你選擇去探索 。
there are unknowns all around us and they're just waiting to be discovered .	我們周圍都有未知的 , 他們只是等待被發現 。

climate change , cosmos , culture , environment , global issues , physics , science , technology , universe	氣候變遷、文化、文化、全球議題、科學、科學、科學、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙、宇宙
david deutsch on our place in the cosmos	大衛在我們宇宙中的地方 。
we've been told to go out on a limb and say something surprising .	我們已經被告知了 , 說一些令人驚訝的事 。
so i'll try and do that , but i want to start with two things that everyone already knows .	所以我要試著做這件事 , 但我想要從兩件事開始 , 大家都知道 。
and the first one , in fact , is something that has been known for most of recorded history .	事實上 , 首先 , 事實上 , 已經被稱為歷史上大部分記錄的歷史 。
and that is that the planet earth , or the solar system , or our environment or whatever , is uniquely suited to sustain our evolution or creation , as it used to be thought and our present existence , and most important , our future survival .	這就是地球 , 或太陽系系統 , 或是太陽系 , 或是我們的環境 , 獨特地保持我們的演化或創造力 , 就像它一樣 , 我們的未來 , 我們的未來存活 , 最重要的 , 我們的未來存活 。
nowadays this idea has a dramatic name: spaceship earth .	現在這個想法有個很戲劇的名字:太空船船 。
and the idea there is that outside the spaceship , the universe is implacably hostile , and inside is all we have , all we depend on .	重點是 , 在太空船上 , 宇宙是不可能的 , 我們都有 , 我們都依賴 。
and we only get the one chance: if we mess up our spaceship , we've got nowhere else to go .	我們只能得到一個機會:如果我們在太空船船上 , 我們就已經沒有其他地方了 。
now , the second thing that everyone already knows is that contrary to what was believed for most of human history , human beings are not , in fact , the hub of existence .	現在 , 大家已經知道的是 , 人類歷史的第二件事 , 人類歷史並不是存在的 , 事實上 , 而是存在存在存在的 。
as stephen hawking famously said , we're just a chemical scum on the surface of a typical planet that's in orbit around a typical star , which is on the outskirts of a typical galaxy , and so on .	史蒂芬哈芬•哈林說 , 我們只是一個典型的化學螢幕表面上有典型的星球表面 , 這是在典型的星系表面上 。
now the first of those two things that everyone knows is kind of saying that we're at a very untypical place , uniquely suited and so on , and the second one is saying that we're at a typical place .	這兩個人都知道 , 我們在一個非常獨特的地方 , 就是說我們在一個非常獨特的地方 , 所以第二個是說我們在一個典型的地方 。
and especially if you regard these two as deep truths to live by and to inform your life decisions , then they seem a little bit to conflict with each other .	尤其是如果你認同這兩者深深處的真相 , 然後他們似乎有點衝突 , 然後他們似乎有點衝突 , 然後他們似乎有點衝突 。

all you've got to do is go a few hundred miles in that same direction and look back , and you won't see any walls or chemical scum at all all you see is a blue planet . and if you go further than that , you'll see the sun , the solar system , and the stars and so on .	你所有人都必須做的是幾百英哩的方向 , 回頭看不到任何牆壁或化學螢光化學螢光 , 你就會看到太陽、太陽系、太陽系、太陽系、太陽系、太陽系、太陽系等等 。

so can we have the lights off , please , so we can see it ?	所以 , 我們能看到燈光 , 請看它嗎 ?
well , not quite , not quite perfect you see , in intergalactic space intergalactic space is completely dark , pitch dark .	嗯 , 不太太完美了 , 國際太空際太空際空間完全黑暗、祈禱的黑暗 。
it's so dark that if you were to be looking at the nearest star to you , and that star were to explode as a supernova , and you were to be staring directly at it at the moment when its light reached you , you still wouldn't be able to see even a glimmer .	所以 , 如果你要仔細觀察最近恆星的星 , 那星星星就會被視為一個超級恐怖 , 而你要盯著它時 , 你仍然無法看見一個玻璃 , 你仍然無法看見一個玻璃 。

and yet from intergalactic space , it's so far away you wouldn't even see it .	但從國際空間中來看 , 遠離你看不到 。

and that is how untypical this place is .	這就是這個地方 。
so can we have the lights back on please ? thank you .	所以 , 我們能否把燈光回來嗎 ? 謝謝 。
now how do we know about an environment that's so far away , and so different , and so alien , from anything we're used to ?	我們要如何了解一個環境 , 遠離我們所知的環境 , 所以不同 , 從我們以前常常常常常見的環境 。
well , the earth our environment , in the form of us is creating knowledge .	我們的環境 , 在我們環境中創造知識 。
well , what does that mean ? well , look out even further than we've just been i mean from here , with a telescope and you'll see things that look like stars .	嗯 , 那意味著什麼 ? 好吧 , 看看我們剛剛從這裡的望遠鏡來看 , 望遠鏡看起來像恆星一樣 。
they're called " quasars . " quasars originally meant quasistellar object .	他們稱之為 「 夸克 」 的品質 。

and we know what they are . billions of years ago , and billions of light years away , the material at the center of a galaxy collapsed towards a supermassive black hole .	我們知道他們在數十億年前 , 光年後 , 數十億光年 , 光是銀河系的黑洞 。
and then intense magnetic fields directed some of the energy of that gravitational collapse . and some of the matter , back out in the form of tremendous jets which illuminated lobes with the brilliance of i think it's a trillion suns .	接著 , 強烈磁場被釋放出一些能量的能量 , 其中一些物質 , 背後的一些物質 , 回到我認為這是一個巨大的珠寶 。 我認為這是一兆兆美元的形式 。
now , the physics of the human brain could hardly be more unlike the physics of such a jet .	現在 , 人類大腦的物理學可以更不像猶太人一樣 。
we couldn't survive for an instant in it . language breaks down when trying to describe what it would be like in one of those jets .	我們不能存活在它語言中倖存下來時 , 語言破壞了 , 當試圖描述這些猶太人之一 。
it would be a bit like experiencing a supernova explosion , but at pointblank range and for millions of years at a time .	它會有點像令人興奮的爆炸 , 但在布朗克朗克朗克朗克朗克朗克朗克朗克朗 , 數百萬年 。
and yet , that jet happened in precisely such a way that billions of years later , on the other side of the universe , some bit of chemical scum could accurately describe , and model , and predict , and explain , above all there's your reference what was happening there , in reality .	然而 , 那個嫉妒發生在數十億年後 , 在宇宙另一邊 , 有些化學螢幕上 , 有些化學螢幕可以準確地描述 , 解釋一下 , 解釋一下 , 解釋一下 , 在現實中 , 解釋一下 , 在現實中發生的事 。
the one physical system , the brain , contains an accurate working model of the other the quasar .	一個身體系統 , 大腦、大腦、持續運作模式的模型模型模型 。
not just a superficial image of it , though it contains that as well , but an explanatory model , embodying the same mathematical relationships and the same causal structure .	不僅僅是超級電腦的影像 , 而是一個解釋模型 , 而是一個解釋模型 , 擁抱相同的數學關係 。
now that is knowledge . and if that weren't amazing enough , the faithfulness with which the one structure resembles the other is increasing with time . that is the growth of knowledge .	這就是知識的知識 , 如果那不夠驚人 , 信仰的信仰 , 另一種結構反對知識的成長 , 那就是知識的成長 。
so , the laws of physics have this special property .	所以 , 物理定律有一個特殊的特徵 。
that physical objects , as unlike each other as they could possibly be , can nevertheless embody the same mathematical and causal structure and to do it more and more so over time .	那個物理物體 , 身為不像他們一樣可能可能永遠都無法放棄同一個數學結構和營養結構 , 更久 。
so we are a chemical scum that is different . this chemical scum has universality .	所以 , 我們是個化學螢幕 , 這種化學螢幕已經不同了 。
its structure contains , with everincreasing precision , the structure of everything . this place , and not other places in the universe , is a hub which contains within itself the structural and causal essence of the whole of the rest of physical reality . and so , far from being insignificant , the fact that the laws of physics allow this , or even mandate that this can happen , is one of the most important things about the physical world .	它結構含有史以來 , 有史以來的基礎結構 , 而不是其他地方 , 而是在宇宙中其他地方 , 而不是其他地方 , 而是在結構和校園中 , 農業和農業之間的存在 。 所以 , 農業和農業之間的存在 。
now how does the solar system and our environment , in the form of us acquire this special relationship with the rest of the universe ?	那麼太陽系和我們的環境 , 在我們的環境中 , 在我們宇宙中的其他特殊關係中 , 其它宇宙的其他部分呢 ?
well , one thing that's true about stephen hawking's remark i mean , it is true , but it's the wrong emphasis . one thing that's true about it is that it doesn't do it with any special physics . there's no special dispensation , no miracles involved . it does it simply with three things that we have here in abundance .	嗯 , 其中一件事情是真正的 , 是真的 , 但它是真的 , 但這是錯的 , 是錯的 , 但它是錯的 , 沒有任何特殊的物理學 。 沒有任何特殊的現象 , 沒有特殊的分佈 。
one of them is matter , because the growth of knowledge is a form of information processing . information processing is computation , computation requires a computer there's no known way of making a computer without matter .	其中之一是很重要的 , 因為知識是一種資訊處理過程 , 資訊過程需要一個電腦處理計算 , 計算需要一台電腦 , 計算需要一台電腦 , 不管如何製造電腦 。
we also need energy to make the computer , and most important , to make the media in effect onto which we record the knowledge that we discover .	我們也需要能源來製造電腦 , 最重要的是 , 我們記錄我們發現的知識 。
and then thirdly , less tangible , but just as essential for the openended creation of knowledge , of explanations , is evidence .	第三 , 不可思議 , 但正如開放的知識 , 只是為了開放知識、解釋、證據 。
now , our environment is inundated with evidence .	我們的環境被證據和證據 。
we happen to get round to testing , let's say , newton's law of gravity about 300 years ago .	我們會繼續測試 , 咱們說 , 新按鈕大約300年前的重力 。
but the evidence that we used to do that was falling down on every square meter of the earth for billions of years before that , and will continue to fall on for billions of years afterwards . and the same is true for all the other sciences .	但證據我們以前所做的證據 , 地球上每平方公尺的證據 , 會持續數十億年後 , 會繼續下降 , 同樣的科學 。
as far as we know , evidence to discover the most fundamental truths of all the sciences is here just for the taking on our planet .	如我們所知 , 證據發現最基本的事實就是為了我們地球上最基本的事實 。
our location is saturated with evidence , and also with matter and energy .	我們的失敗是充滿證據的證據 , 也和能量 。
out in intergalactic space , those three prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge are at their lowest possible supply .	在國際公共空間中 , 有三位預防的知識是最低的創造力 。
as i said , it's empty ; it's cold ; and it's dark out there . or is it ?	如我說 , 這真是空的 ; 冷卻了 。 還是黑暗出來嗎 ?
now actually , that's just another parochial misconception .	事實上 , 這只是另一個父母誤解 。
because imagine a cube out there in intergalactic space , the same size as our home , the solar system . now that cube is very empty by human standards , but that still means that it contains over a million tons of matter .	因為想像一下 , 在國際空間中 , 如我們的家園一樣大 , 太陽系的太陽系一樣大 , 但這仍然意味著它存在超過一百萬噸的重要性 。
and a million tons is enough to make , say , a selfcontained space station , on which there's a colony of scientists that are devoted to creating an openended stream of knowledge , and so on .	一百萬噸噸的確有足夠的太空站 , 說 , 一個自動的科學家 , 創造出一個開放的知識 , 來創造一個開放的知識 , 等等 。
now , it's way beyond present technology to even gather the hydrogen from intergalactic space and form it into other elements and so on .	現在 , 科技是超越國際空間 , 甚至將氫氣中的氫氣 , 形成其他元素 , 形成其他元素和其他元素 。
but the thing is , in a comprehensible universe , if something isn't forbidden by the laws of physics , then what could possibly prevent us from doing it , other than knowing how ?	但重點是 , 在一個物理定律中 , 如果某件事不可思議的宇宙法律 , 那麼可能可能可能可能預防我們做這件事 , 不管我們做什麼 ?
in other words , it's a matter of knowledge , not resources .	換句話說 , 這是個知識 , 不是資源 。
and the same well , if we could do that we'd automatically have an energy supply , because the transmutation would be a fusion reactor and evidence ?	同樣的 , 如果我們能做到這一點 , 我們就可以自動駕駛反應爐 , 因為移植反應會是核心反應爐和證據 ?
well , again , it's dark out there to human senses . but all you've got to do is take a telescope , even one of presentday design , look out and you'll see the same galaxies as we do from here .	再一次 , 人類感官是黑暗的 , 但你所有人感官設計的望遠鏡 , 即使在今天的設計中 , 你就會看到同樣的星系 。
and with a more powerful telescope , you'll be able to see stars , and planets .	隨著更強大的望遠鏡 , 你就能看到星星星星、星球 。
in those galaxies , you'll be able to do astrophysics , and learn the laws of physics .	在那些銀河系中 , 你就能做到物理定律 , 學習物理定律 。
and locally there you could build particle accelerators , and learn elementary particle physics , and chemistry , and so on .	當地地 , 你可以建造粒子物理粒子 , 學習元素 , 學習元素、化學物質、化學物質、化學物質、等等 。
probably the hardest science to do would be biology field trips because it would take several hundred million years to get to the nearest lifebearing planet and back .	可能是生物學領域最困難的科學 , 因為它會花了數百萬年的時間才能到最近的生命 。
but i have to tell you and sorry , richard but i never did like biology field trips much , and i think we can just about make do with one every few hundred million years .	但我必須告訴各位 , 抱歉 , 但我從來沒有像生物學領域試驗 , 我認為我們可以用一百萬年的時間做 。
so in fact , intergalactic space does contain all the prerequisites for the openended creation of knowledge . any such cube , anywhere in the universe , could become the same kind of hub that we are , if the knowledge of how to do so were present there .	所以事實上 , 國際空間不會持續所有準備好的設備 , 任何地方都可以成為知識的知識 。 宇宙中任何地方 , 都有可能成為我們現在所處的幽默 , 如果知識知識知識如何做到 。
so we're not in a uniquely hospitable place .	所以我們不是獨特的地方 。
if intergalactic space is capable of creating an openended stream of explanations , then so is almost every other environment . so is the earth . so is a polluted earth .	如果國際公共空間可以創造一個開放的解釋 , 那麼幾乎是其他環境 。 所以幾乎是地球 。 所以 , 地球是污染的 。 所以 , 就是污染了地球 。
and the limiting factor , there and here , is not resources , because they're plentiful , but knowledge , which is scarce .	限制工廠 , 這裡沒有資源 , 因為他們是很聰明 , 但知識 , 知識是很嚇人 。
now this cosmic knowledgebased view may and i think ought to make us feel very special . but it should also make us feel vulnerable , because it means that without the specific knowledge that's needed to survive the ongoing challenges of the universe , we won't survive them .	現在這個宇宙知識的觀點 , 我認為它是非常特別的 。 但它也應該讓我們感到脆弱 , 因為它意味著沒有特定的知識 , 因為它意味著沒有特定知識的知識 , 我們也不會存活下來 。
all it takes is for a supernova to go off a few light years away , and we'll all be dead !	一切都花了幾小時的時間 , 我們都死了 , 我們都死了 !
martin rees has recently written a book about our vulnerability to all sorts of things , from astrophysics , to scientific experiments gone wrong , and most importantly to terrorism with weapons of mass destruction .	馬丁最近寫了一本關於我們脆弱的書籍 , 從物理學、科學實驗、科學實驗 , 最重要的是恐怖主義實驗 , 最重要的是恐怖主義的武器 。
and he thinks that civilization has only a 50 percent chance of surviving this century .	他認為文明只有百分之五十的機會 。
i think he's going to talk about that later in the conference .	我想他會談到那之後 , 在會議中 。
now i don't think that probability is the right category to discuss this issue in .	現在我不認為 , 可能是正確的 , 就是要討論這個議題 。
but i do agree with him about this . we can survive , and we can fail to survive .	但我和他有關這一點 , 我們可以存活下來 , 我們可以無法存活下來 。
but it depends not on chance , but on whether we create the relevant knowledge in time .	但它依賴沒有機會 , 但無論我們創造出的重要知識 。
the danger is not at all unprecedented . species go extinct all the time .	危險並不是全部都被忽略了物種 。
civilizations end . the overwhelming majority of all species and all civilizations that have ever existed are now history .	文明最終 。 文明結束了所有物種和所有文明的文明 , 現在已經存在了歷史 。
and if we want to be the exception to that , then logically our only hope is to make use of the one feature that distinguishes our species , and our civilization , from all the others namely , our special relationship with the laws of physics , our ability to create new explanations , new knowledge to be a hub of existence .	如果我們想要成為這個展覽 , 那麼邏輯地 , 邏輯地 , 我們唯一希望的是要用一種特殊的特徵 , 我們的文明 , 我們的文明 , 我們的文明 , 我們的文明 , 創造新的解釋 , 新的知識 , 我們的能力 , 創造出新的形式 。
so let me now apply this to a current controversy , not because i want to advocate any particular solution , but just to illustrate the kind of thing i mean .	讓我來看看目前的爭議 , 不是因為我想要投票任何特定的解決方案 , 但我只想把任何特定的解決方案 。
and the controversy is global warming .	而爭議是全球暖化的 。
now , i'm a physicist , but i'm not the right kind of physicist . in regard to global warming , i'm just a layman . and the rational thing for a layman to do is to take seriously the prevailing scientific theory . and according to that theory , it's already too late to avoid a disaster .	現在 , 我是個物理學家 , 但我不是對全球暖化學家的權利主義者
because if it's true that our best option at the moment is to prevent co2 emissions with something like the kyoto protocol , with its constraints on economic activity and its enormous cost of hundreds of billions of dollars or whatever it is , then that is already a disaster by any reasonable measure .	因為如果是真的 , 我們最好的選項是預防二氧化碳排放 , 和經濟活動相對的經濟活動有相當大的成本 , 其限於經濟活動上百億美元或不論是任何理由的測量
and the actions that are advocated are not even purported to solve the problem , merely to postpone it by a little . so it's already too late to avoid it , and it probably has been too late to avoid it ever since before anyone realized the danger .	而行動的行動 , 甚至沒有被迫害解決問題 , 幾乎無法避免這個問題 , 所以它已經太遲了 , 所以它已經太遲了 。 所以它可能已經太遲了 , 因為任何人意識到危險之前 , 任何人意識到危險 。
it was probably already too late in the 1970s , when the best available scientific theory was telling us that industrial emissions were about to precipitate a new ice age in which billions would die .	它可能已經太遲了 , 在1970年代最好的科學理論是告訴我們 , 工業排放一個新的冰箱 。
now the lesson of that seems clear to me , and i don't know why it isn't informing public debate .	現在這似乎很清楚 , 我不知道為什麼它沒有改革公共辯論 。
it is that we can't always know . when we know of an impending disaster , and how to solve it at a cost less than the cost of the disaster itself , then there's not going to be much argument , really .	我們永遠無法永遠知道 。 當我們知道一個改善災難時 , 我們要如何解決它的成本 , 如何解決災難本身的成本 , 其實沒有太多的論點 。
but no precautions , and no precautionary principle , can avoid problems that we do not yet foresee .	但沒有預防 , 沒有預防的原則 , 可以避免的問題 , 避免我們還沒忘記 。
hence , we need a stance of problemfixing , not just problemavoidance .	嗯 , 我們需要解決問題 , 不僅僅是重大的問題 。

the world is buzzing at the moment with plans to force reductions in gas emissions at all costs .	世界在氣體中被迫害的時刻 , 迫使氣體排放 。

and with problems that we are not aware of yet , the ability to put right not the sheer good luck of avoiding indefinitely is our only hope , not just of solving problems , but of survival .	我們還沒有意識到的問題 , 而不是她更好的能力 , 而是生存的能力 , 而是我們的唯一希望 , 不只是解決問題 , 而是存活的問題 , 而是生存問題 。

it poses a very fascinating puzzle for us .	對我們來說 , 它很棒的謎題 。
these african students are doing their homework under streetlights at the airport in the capital city because they don't have any electricity at home .	這些非洲學生正在做他們的家鄉在街上飛機場 , 因為他們沒有任何電力 。
now , i haven't met these particular students , but i've met students like them .	現在 , 我沒有遇到這些特別的學生 , 但我遇到像他們一樣 。

why is it that nelson has access to a cuttingedge technology , like the cellphone , but doesn't have access to a 100yearold technology for generating electric light in the home ?	為什麼 , nelon必須取得剪斷技術 , 就像手機手機手機一樣 , 但沒有用到100歲的科技 , 可以在家裡產生電燈光的電燈 ?

bad rules can prevent the kind of winwin solution that's available when people can bring new technologies in and make them available to someone like nelson .	壞規則可以防止新技術 , 讓人們能夠把新科技帶到像nelonon一樣 , 讓他們像nelonononon一樣 。
what kinds of rules ?	什麼規則呢 ?
the electric company in this nation operates under a rule , which says that it has to sell electricity at a very low , subsidized price in fact , a price that is so low it loses money on every unit that it sells .	在這個國家的電廠公司中電力公司 , 也就是說它必須賣電力的價格 , 事實上 , 一個價格的價格 , 價格的價格 。
so it has neither the resources , nor the incentives , to hook up many other users .	所以它有資源 , 沒有獎勵 , 沒有獎勵的人 。
the president wanted to change this rule .	總統想要改變這個規則 。
he's seen that it's possible to have a different set of rules , rules where businesses earn a small profit , so they have an incentive to sign up more customers .	他看過 , 可能有不同的規則 , 企業早期的規則 , 企業耳其有獎勵 , 所以他們有獎勵的客戶 。
that's the kind of rules that the cellphone company that nelson purchases his telephony from operates under .	這就是手機公司的規則 , nelonpurchasonpurchassonpurchassonysony的規則 。
the president has seen how those rules worked well .	總統已經看過這些規則是如何運作的 。
so he tried to change the rules for pricing on electricity , but ran into a firestorm of protest from businesses and consumers who wanted to preserve the existing subsidized rates .	所以他試著改變電力的規則 , 但他進入商業和消費者們想要保存現有的抗議率 。
so he was stuck with rules that prevented him from letting the winwin solution help his country .	所以他被困擾了他國家的規則 , 讓他的國家能夠協助他的國家 。
and nelson is stuck studying under the streetlights .	尼爾森在街上被困在街上 。
the real challenge then , is to try to figure out how we can change rules .	真正的挑戰是 , 試著找出我們要如何改變規則 。
are there some rules we can develop for changing rules ?	有一些規則我們可以為改變規則嗎 ?
i want to argue that there is a general abstract insight that we can make practical , which is that , if we can give more choices to people , and more choices to leaders who , in many countries , are also people .	我想說 , 有一個一般的抽象 , 我們可以做出實際的抽象 , 也就是說 , 如果我們能給更多選擇更多選擇 , 更多選擇領導人 , 更多選擇領導人 , 同時也就是人們 。
but , it's useful to present the opposition between these two .	但 , 這兩者之間很有用 。
because the kind of choice you might want to give to a leader , a choice like giving the president the choice to raise prices on electricity , takes away a choice that people in the economy want .	因為你可能想要給領導者 , 像是提供總統的選擇 , 像是在電力上提供的選擇 , 讓經濟的選擇 。
they want the choice to be able to continue consuming subsidized electric power .	他們希望能夠持續消費電力的選擇 。
so if you give just to one side or the other , you'll have tension or friction .	所以如果你給一邊或另一邊 , 你就會有緊張或犯罪 。
but if we can find ways to give more choices to both , that will give us a set of rules for changing rules that get us out of traps .	但如果我們能找到更多選擇的方法 , 那將會給我們一個規則的規則 , 讓我們脫離陷陷阱的規則 。
now , nelson also has access to the internet .	現在 , nelon也能取得網路 。

when they separated , they made choices that led to very divergent paths for their sets of rules .	當他們分開時 , 他們做出選擇 , 導致規則的多樣性 。

what haiti warns us is that rules can be bad because governments are weak .	海地戰爭是我們弱勢的規則 , 因為政府是弱勢 。

now , china dramatically demonstrates both the potential and the challenges of working with rules .	現在 , 中國巨大的潛力和規則的潛力和規則合作 。
back in the beginning of the data presented in this chart , china was the world's hightechnology leader .	回到這個鏈的開始 , 中國是世界上最高科技領導人 。

income there stayed stagnant , as it zoomed ahead in the rest of the world .	克服在那裡 , 當它放棄了世界上其他地方 。

growth took off in china . the chinese started catching up very quickly with the united states .	成長在中國 , 中國開始捕撈 , 中國開始捕撈 。
