but if you don't know why you do what you do , and people respond to why you do what you do , then how will you ever get people to vote for you , or buy something from you , or , more importantly , be loyal and want to be a part of what it is that you do .	但如果你不知道你為什麼做的事 , 人們對你做的事 , 人們對你做的事 , 那麼你要如何讓人們參與投票 , 或者更重要的是 , 或是更重要的是 , 孤獨 , 或是更重要的是你所做的 。
again , the goal is not just to sell to people who need what you have ; the goal is to sell to people who believe what you believe .	再一次 , 目標不僅要賣你誰需要什麼 ; 目標是要賣你相信你所相信的 。
the goal is not just to hire people who need a job ; it's to hire people who believe what you believe .	目標不只是要僱用那些需要工作的人 , 而是要僱用那些相信你所相信的 。
i always say that , you know , if you hire people just because they can do a job , they'll work for your money , but if you hire people who believe what you believe , they'll work for you with blood and sweat and tears .	我總是說 , 如果你僱用人們只是因為他們能做工作 , 他們會為你的錢工作 , 但如果你僱用血液和甜甜甜味的人 。
and nowhere else is there a better example of this than with the wright brothers .	其他地方還有更好的例子 , 比起兄弟弟弟 。
most people don't know about samuel pierpont langley .	大多數人不知道香港的責任 。
and back in the early 20th century , the pursuit of powered man flight was like the dot com of the day .	回到20世紀初 , 普通人飛行的旅程 , 如今 , 如今日的最佳收入 。
everybody was trying it .	每個人都在嘗試它 。
and samuel pierpont langley had , what we assume , to be the recipe for success .	而amuelpsontlangley的確是假設成功的 。
i mean , even now , you ask people , " why did your product or why did your company fail ? "	甚至現在 , 你問人們: 「 為什麼你的產品或為什麼你的產品失敗 ? 」
and people always give you the same permutation of the same three things: undercapitalized , the wrong people , bad market conditions .	人們總是給你同樣的感覺:在意外化、壞市場條件、壞市場條件、壞市場條件 。
it's always the same three things , so let's explore that .	它總是相同三件事 , 所以我們來探究這一點 。
samuel pierpont langley was given 50 , 000 dollars by the war department to figure out this flying machine .	amuelpleyontlangley被送到50000美金來找出這個飛行器
money was no problem .	錢不是問題 。
he held a seat at harvard and worked at the smithsonian and was extremely wellconnected ; he knew all the big minds of the day .	他在哈佛遜和史密森一起工作 , 在米爾森和工作工作中工作 , 他知道所有人的大思想 。
he hired the best minds money could find and the market conditions were fantastic .	他僱用最好的思想 , 市場條件是很棒的 。
the new york times followed him around everywhere , and everyone was rooting for langley .	紐約時報的紐約時報 , 每個人都在追蹤他 。
then how come we've never heard of samuel pierpont langley ?	那麼 , 我們怎麼從來沒有聽過amuel監獄 ?
a few hundred miles away in dayton ohio , orville and wilbur wright , they had none of what we consider to be the recipe for success .	幾百英里遠遠遠遠遠超過幾百英哩 , 他們沒有我們所認為的成功 。
they had no money ; they paid for their dream with the proceeds from their bicycle shop ; not a single person on the wright brothers' team had a college education , not even orville or wilbur ; and the new york times followed them around nowhere .	他們沒有錢 , 他們為他們的夢想 , 和他們的夢想 , 不是單一人在最高的兄弟 , 而是一個大學的大學教育 , 甚至紐約時報或wilbur ; 甚至紐約時報或wilbur ; 紐約時報的新聞報導 。
the difference was , orville and wilbur were driven by a cause , by a purpose , by a belief .	差別是 , 橘色和翅膀被驅動的原因 , 由一個信念 。
they believed that if they could figure out this flying machine , it'll change the course of the world .	他們相信如果他們能找出這個飛行機器 , 它會改變世界的過程 。
samuel pierpont langley was different .	amuelpley是不同的 。
he wanted to be rich , and he wanted to be famous .	他想要富裕 , 他想要有名名的 。
he was in pursuit of the result .	他在追求結果 。
he was in pursuit of the riches .	他在富裕的監獄中 。
and lo and behold , look what happened .	洛杉磯 , 看看發生了什麼事 。
the people who believed in the wright brothers' dream worked with them with blood and sweat and tears .	那些相信在最糟糕的兄弟夢想與他們一起合作 。
the others just worked for the paycheck .	其他人只是為了付錢 。
and they tell stories of how every time the wright brothers went out , they would have to take five sets of parts , because that's how many times they would crash before they came in for supper .	他們告訴大家 , 每次最糟糕的兄弟們 , 他們必須花五個部分 , 因為這是他們在供供應器上 , 因為那有多少次他們在供應器上 。
and , eventually , on december 17th , 1903 , the wright brothers took flight , and no one was there to even experience it .	最終 , 在12月17日11月17日 , 1903日 , 沒有人會飛行 , 沒有人會經歷過它 。
we found out about it a few days later .	我們發現這幾天後 ,
and further proof that langley was motivated by the wrong thing: the day the wright brothers took flight , he quit .	更進一步的教授 , 是錯誤的:那天那天最棒的兄弟們帶著飛機 , 他安靜 。
he could have said , " that's an amazing discovery , guys , and i will improve upon your technology , " but he didn't .	他可以說說: 「 這是個很棒的發現 , 傢伙 , 我會改善你的科技 , 」 但他沒有 。
he wasn't first , he didn't get rich , he didn't get famous so he quit .	他不是首先 , 他沒有錢錢 , 他沒有錢 , 所以他辭掉了 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 , 他們買了為什麼你這樣做 。
and if you talk about what you believe , you will attract those who believe what you believe .	如果你談論你所相信的 , 你會吸引那些相信你所相信的 。
but why is it important to attract those who believe what you believe ?	但為什麼要吸引那些相信你相信什麼 ?
something called the law of diffusion of innovation , and if you don't know the law , you definitely know the terminology .	一種叫做 「 創新 」 的法律 , 如果你不知道法律 , 你絕對不知道法律學 。
the first two and a half percent of our population are our innovators .	首先 , 我們的人口是創新者 。
the next 13 and a half percent of our population are our early adopters .	下一個13% , 我們的人口是早期的 。
the next 34 percent are your early majority , your late majority and your laggards .	下一個34%是你的早期 , 你的遲早 , 你的女士 。
the only reason these people buy touch tone phones is because you can't buy rotary phones anymore .	這些人買到手機的唯一原因是因為你不能買浪費手機 。
we all sit at various places at various times on this scale , but what the law of diffusion of innovation tells us is that if you want massmarket success or massmarket acceptance of an idea , you cannot have it until you achieve this tipping point between 15 and 18 percent market penetration , and then the system tips .	我們都坐在這個規模上 , 在這個規模上 , 但在創新告訴我們 , 如果你想要大麻的執行方式告訴我們 , 若你想要大麻或大屠殺的概念 , 你就不能完成這個組織 , 直到15%和18%的市場之間 , 直到18%和18%的市場之間 。
and i love asking businesses , " what's your conversion on new business ? "	我喜歡問企業: 「 你的內容是什麼 ? 」
and they love to tell you , " oh , it's about 10 percent , " proudly .	他們很喜歡告訴你們: 「 喔 , 這是大約10% 。 」 很驕傲 。
well , you can trip over 10 percent of the customers .	嗯 , 你可以試過超過10%的客戶 。
we all have about 10 percent who just " get it . "	我們都有大約百分之十 。
that's how we describe them , right ?	這就是我們如何描述它們 , 對吧 ?
that's like that gut feeling , " oh , they just get it . "	這就像那種猜猜想: 「 喔 , 他們只是拿到它 。 」
the problem is: how do you find the ones that get it before you're doing business with them versus the ones who don't get it ?	問題是:你要如何找到它 , 你要如何找到它 ?
so it's this here , this little gap that you have to close , as jeffrey moore calls it , " crossing the chasm " because , you see , the early majority will not try something until someone else has tried it first .	這裡是這裡的 , 這是你必須靠近的 , 如傑夫•摩爾稱之為 「 雲朵 」 因為你看到的 , 早期 , 最早就不會嘗試任何人試驗 。
and these guys , the innovators and the early adopters , they're comfortable making those gut decisions .	而這些傢伙 , 創新者和早期的選項 , 他們很舒服的決定 。
they're more comfortable making those intuitive decisions that are driven by what they believe about the world and not just what product is available .	他們更有舒適的決定 , 是因為他們所相信的世界 , 不僅是生產力的 。
these are the people who stood in line for six hours to buy an iphone when they first came out , when you could have just walked into the store the next week and bought one off the shelf .	這些是那些站在六小時內買一台iphone時 , 買了一台iphone , 當他們第一次走出來時 , 買了一台iphone 。
these are the people who spent 40 , 000 dollars on flat screen tvs when they first came out , even though the technology was substandard .	這些是花了40000美金的電視機 , 儘管他們第一次出去 , 即使科技被主宰了 。
and , by the way , they didn't do it because the technology was so great ; they did it for themselves .	順便一提 , 他們不這麼做是因為科技很棒 , 他們為自己做自己做 。
it's because they wanted to be first .	因為他們想要成為首先 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it and what you do simply proves what you believe .	人們不買你的事 , 他們買了為什麼你做這件事 , 你只能證明你所相信的 。
in fact , people will do the things that prove what they believe .	事實上 , 人們會做他們所相信的事物 。
the reason that person bought the iphone in the first six hours , stood in line for six hours , was because of what they believed about the world , and how they wanted everybody to see them: they were first .	第一六小時 , 有人買了iphone的原因是 , 站在六小時內 , 是因為他們相信這個世界 , 而他們想要每個人都看到他們是第一 。
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it .	人們不買你做的事 , 他們買了為什麼你這樣做 。
so let me give you a famous example , a famous failure and a famous success of the law of diffusion of innovation .	讓我給各位一個很有名的失敗和一位有名的失敗和一位有名的成功 。
first , the famous failure .	首先 , 很有名的失敗
it's a commercial example .	這是商業例子 。
as we said before , a second ago , the recipe for success is money and the right people and the right market conditions , right ? you should have success then .	如同我們之前所說的 , 成功是錢和正確的市場條件 , 對吧 ? 你應該成功 。
from the time tivo came out about eight or nine years ago to this current day , they are the single highestquality product on the market , hands down , there is no dispute .	從198年開始 , 大約有八歲或九年前 , 他們是市場上最高品質產品 , 沒有輸入 。
they were extremely wellfunded .	他們非常受傷 。
market conditions were fantastic .	市場條件很棒 。
i mean , we use tivo as verb .	我的意思是 , 我們用抗拒 。
i tivo stuff on my piece of junk time warner dvr all the time .	我每次在叢林上抗議時 , 我把這些東西放到dvrvr 。
but tivo's a commercial failure .	但tivovo是商業失敗 。
they've never made money .	他們從來沒有賺錢 。
and when they went ipo , their stock was at about 30 or 40 dollars and then plummeted , and it's never traded above 10 .	當他們走到ipo時 , 他們的股票大約有30到40美元 , 然後它從來沒有被吸引到10歲 。
in fact , i don't think it's even traded above six , except for a couple of little spikes .	事實上 , 我不認為它甚至是6 , ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~ ~
because you see , when tivo launched their product they told us all what they had .	因為你看到 , 當抗拒他們產品時 , 他們告訴我們他們他們的東西 。
they said , " we have a product that pauses live tv , skips commercials , rewinds live tv and memorizes your viewing habits without you even asking . "	他們說: 「 我們有一份產品 」 的產品 , 技巧、技巧、技能、電視和記憶力 , 不管你甚至問你 。 」
and the cynical majority said , " we don't believe you .	而循環主要說: 「 我們不相信你 。 」
we don't need it . we don't like it .	我們不需要 。 我們不喜歡它 。
you're scaring us . "	你害怕我們 。 」
what if they had said , " if you're the kind of person who likes to have total control over every aspect of your life , boy , do we have a product for you .	如果他們說: 「 如果你是你人生中的一種人 , 男孩們必須控制你的人生 , 男孩們 , 我們有產品給你一個產品 。
it pauses live tv , skips commercials , memorizes your viewing habits , etc . , etc . "	它保留電視、技巧、技巧、技巧、記憶、等等 。 」
people don't buy what you do ; they buy why you do it , and what you do simply serves as the proof of what you believe .	人們不買你做的事 , 他們買了為什麼你這樣做 , 你只是把你當作服務當成你所相信的 。
now let me give you a successful example of the law of diffusion of innovation .	現在讓我給各位一個成功的例子 。
in the summer of 1963 , 250 , 000 people showed up on the mall in washington to hear dr . king speak .	1963年夏天夏天夏天的夏天 , 在華盛頓大廳裡 , 有250000人在華盛頓國王 。
they sent out no invitations , and there was no website to check the date .	他們從沒有邀請 , 沒有網站去檢查 , 沒有網站來檢查 。
how do you do that ?	你怎麼做 ?
well , dr . king wasn't the only man in america who was a great orator .	嗯 , 王國不僅是美國最棒的人 。

and people who believed what he believed took his cause , and they made it their own , and they told people .	而那些相信他所相信的原因 , 讓他們自己的原因 , 他們告訴別人他自己 , 他們告訴別人 。

it's what they believed about america that got them to travel in a bus for eight hours to stand in the sun in washington in the middle of august .	這是他們所相信的美國 , 讓他們在華盛頓大學中旅行八小時 , 站在華盛頓頓的中間 。
it's what they believed , and it wasn't about black versus white: 25 percent of the audience was white .	這是他們所相信的 , 而不是黑人版本白:25%的觀眾是白人 。
dr . king believed that there are two types of laws in this world: those that are made by a higher authority and those that are made by man .	博士相信這世界上有兩種法律的法律:那些是由男人製造出來的 。
and not until all the laws that are made by man are consistent with the laws that are made by the higher authority will we live in a just world .	直到所有法律的法律 , 直到所有法律的法律 , 我們將生活在一個世界中 。
it just so happened that the civil rights movement was the perfect thing to help him bring his cause to life .	剛剛剛剛剛剛剛剛好的事 , 讓他帶領他的原因 。
we followed , not for him , but for ourselves .	我們追蹤了 , 不是為了自己 , 而是為了自己 。
and , by the way , he gave the " i have a dream " speech , not the " i have a plan " speech .	順便一提 , 他給了 「 我有一個夢想 」 , 不是 「 我有計劃 」 。
listen to politicians now , with their comprehensive 12point plans .	現在傾聽政治家人現在 , 他們的競爭計畫 。

because there are leaders and there are those who lead .	因為有領導人和領導人 。
leaders hold a position of power or authority , but those who lead inspire us .	領導者有權力或權權力 , 但那些領導我們鼓舞我們 。
whether they're individuals or organizations , we follow those who lead , not because we have to , but because we want to .	無論他們是個人或組織 , 我們遵循那些領導的人 , 而是因為我們想要的 。
we follow those who lead , not for them , but for ourselves .	我們遵循那些領導的人 , 而不是為了自己 。
and it's those who start with " why " that have the ability to inspire those around them or find others who inspire them .	這是那些從 「 為何 」 的能力來啟發這些人的能力 , 或是找到其他靈感的人 。
how do you remember where you parked your car ? how do you know if you're moving in the right direction ? neuroscientist neil burgess studies the neural mechanisms that map the space around us , and how they link to memory and imagination .	你要如何記住你的車子 ? 你要如何知道你在右邊移動 ? 神經科學學家neil燃燒的研究呢 ? 神經科學學家尼爾•尼爾文學家 , 他們如何連結我們周圍的空間 ?
brain , cognitive science , exploration , neuroscience , science	大腦、認知科學、探索、探索、神經科學、神經科學、科學、科學、科學、科學、科學、科學、
neil burgess: how your brain tells you where you are	neil負責:你的大腦告訴你你在哪裡 ?
when we park in a big parking lot , how do we remember where we parked our car ?	當我們在大停車裡時 , 我們要如何記得我們把車子放在哪裡 ?
here's the problem facing homer .	這是一個問題的回家 。
and we're going to try to understand what's happening in his brain .	我們要試著了解他的大腦發生什麼事 。
so we'll start with the hippocampus , shown in yellow , which is the organ of memory .	所以我們從山坡開始 , ypocampus , 這是記憶體的器官 。
if you have damage there , like in alzheimer's , you can't remember things including where you parked your car .	如果你有損害 , 就像阿茲海默症一樣 , 你可以記住你的車輛 。
it's named after latin for " seahorse , " which it resembles .	它被稱為 「 海水後 」 的名字 「 海水 」 的名字 。
and like the rest of the brain , it's made of neurons .	就像大腦其他的其他部分 , 它是由神經元組成的 。
so the human brain has about a hundred billion neurons in it .	所以人類的大腦有大約一百億個神經元 。
and the neurons communicate with each other by sending little pulses or spikes of electricity via connections to each other .	而神經元溝通彼此溝通 , 透過電力來傳遞一些小型脈絡 , 來彼此互聯繫 。
the hippocampus is formed of two sheets of cells , which are very densely interconnected .	山丘形成了兩塊細胞 , 非常密切的細胞 , 非常密切地連結 。
and scientists have begun to understand how spatial memory works by recording from individual neurons in rats or mice while they forage or explore an environment looking for food .	科學家們必須了解脊椎記憶如何運作 , 透過個人神經元的記錄 , 或他們為年齡或花費時間去探索食物 。
so we're going to imagine we're recording from a single neuron in the hippocampus of this rat here .	所以 , 我們要想像我們從一個單一神經元的記錄 。
and when it fires a little spike of electricity , there's going to be a red dot and a click .	當它消防了電力時 , 就會變成紅點的紅點 , 就會變成紅點 。
so what we see is that this neuron knows whenever the rat has gone into one particular place in its environment .	所以我們所看到的是 , 當種族歧視的神經元已經進入了一個特定的地方 。
and it signals to the rest of the brain by sending a little electrical spike .	它的訊號 , 傳送大腦的另一半電晶片 。
so we could show the firing rate of that neuron as a function of the animal's location .	我們可以展示這些神經元作為動物的功能 。
and if we record from lots of different neurons , we'll see that different neurons fire when the animal goes in different parts of its environment , like in this square box shown here .	如果我們從許多不同的神經元 , 我們會看到不同神經元時 , 我們會看到這些不同的神經元 , 就像這平方方盒一樣 。
so together they form a map for the rest of the brain , telling the brain continually , " where am i now within my environment ? "	他們一起形成一個大腦地圖的地圖 , 告訴大腦持續在哪裡 ? 」
place cells are also being recorded in humans .	細胞也被記錄在人類身上 。
so epilepsy patients sometimes need the electrical activity in their brain monitoring .	所以癲癇患者有時需要電動動活動 。
and some of these patients played a video game where they drive around a small town .	有些病人在玩耍遊戲中 , 他們在一個小鎮上 , 他們在一個小鎮上 。
and place cells in their hippocampi would fire , become active , start sending electrical impulses whenever they drove through a particular location in that town .	細胞裡的細胞細胞會消防 , 變成活躍 , 開始發送電電池時 , 開始發送電電池 。
so how does a place cell know where the rat or person is within its environment ?	那麼一個細胞怎麼知道種族或人在環境中 ?
well these two cells here show us that the boundaries of the environment are particularly important .	這兩個細胞告訴我們 , 環境非常重要 。
so the one on the top likes to fire sort of midway between the walls of the box that their rat's in .	所以 , 最頂端的盒子 , 把他們的種族隔離 。
and when you expand the box , the firing location expands .	當你擴大盒時 , 飛行器會擴展擴展擴展 。
the one below likes to fire whenever there's a wall close by to the south .	其中一個樹木時 , 一個是南方的牆壁接近 。
and if you put another wall inside the box , then the cell fires in both place wherever there's a wall to the south as the animal explores around in its box .	如果你把另一個牆放在盒子裡 , 那麼細胞會消防在盒子裡有一個牆壁的牆壁 。
so this predicts that sensing the distances and directions of boundaries around you extended buildings and so on is particularly important for the hippocampus .	所以這預測顯示在你周圍的距離和方向的距離 , 尤其重要的是 , 隱藏建築物的重要性 。
and indeed , on the inputs to the hippocampus , cells are found which project into the hippocampus , which do respond exactly to detecting boundaries or edges at particular distances and directions from the rat or mouse as it's exploring around .	的確 , 在山丘上 , 細胞被發現 , 細胞被視為隱藏的隱藏 , 細胞在特定的距離 , 或被視為特定的距離和方向的位置 。
so the cell on the left , you can see , it fires whenever the animal gets near to a wall or a boundary to the east , whether it's the edge or the wall of a square box or the circular wall of the circular box or even the drop at the edge of a table , which the animals are running around .	所以左邊的細胞 , 你可以看到 , 它會消防在東邊或一磅重 , 不論是邊緣或圓形的牆壁或牆壁牆壁的牆壁 , 或甚至在桌子上 , 動物在桌子上跑 。
and the cell on the right there fires whenever there's a boundary to the south , whether it's the drop at the edge of the table or a wall or even the gap between two tables that are pulled apart .	在右邊的細胞上 , 每當有一磅的細胞 , 不論是桌子或牆壁或牆壁或牆壁之間的差距 。
so that's one way in which we think place cells determine where the animal is as it's exploring around .	這就是我們認為細胞決定哪些細胞決定哪裡 ?
we can also test where we think objects are , like this goal flag , in simple environments or indeed , where your car would be .	我們也能測試我們認為物體就像這個目標一樣 , 在簡單的環境中 , 你的車子會在哪裡 。
so we can have people explore an environment and see the location they have to remember .	我們可以有人探索一個環境 , 看到他們必須記住他們 。
and then , if we put them back in the environment , generally they're quite good at putting a marker down where they thought that flag or their car was .	然後 , 如果我們把它們放在環境中 , 通常他們認為旗幟或車子 , 他們認為旗幟或車子 。
but on some trials , we could change the shape and size of the environment like we did with the place cell .	但在某些試驗中 , 我們可以改變細胞的形狀和大小的環境 。
in that case , we can see how where they think the flag had been changes as a function of how you change the shape and size of the environment .	在那個情況下 , 我們可以看到旗幟如何認為旗幟的形狀和環境的大小改變 。
and what you see , for example , if the flag was where that cross was in a small square environment , and then if you ask people where it was , but you've made the environment bigger , where they think the flag had been stretches out in exactly the same way that the place cell firing stretched out .	舉例來說 , 如果你問旗幟在一個小平方環境中 , 就在一個小平方環境中 , 但如果你問人們 , 你就會覺得旗幟很大 , 但你讓旗幟變得更大 。
it's as if you remember where the flag was by storing the pattern of firing across all of your place cells at that location , and then you can get back to that location by moving around so that you best match the current pattern of firing of your place cells with that stored pattern .	就像你記得在哪裡的旗幟被儲存的圖案 , 然後你可以回到那個地方的細胞 , 然後你可以回到那個地方 , 然後你就可以回到那個地方 , 最好的配合模式 。
that guides you back to the location that you want to remember .	你回溯到你想要記得的位置 。
but we also know where we are through movement .	但我們也知道我們在哪裡 。
so if we take some outbound path perhaps we park and we wander off we know because our own movements , which we can integrate over this path roughly what the heading direction is to go back .	所以如果我們拿一些外面的路徑 , 我們就會知道 , 因為自己的運動 , 我們可以把這個路徑放進這個路徑 , 我們就可以把頭部放回來 。
and place cells also get this kind of path integration input from a kind of cell called a grid cell .	細胞也能得到這種病例 , 從一種叫做 「 圖細胞細胞 」 的細胞 。
now grid cells are found , again , on the inputs to the hippocampus , and they're a bit like place cells .	現在圖細胞發現 , 再一次 , 輸入到山坡上 , 他們有點像細胞一樣 。
but now as the rat explores around , each individual cell fires in a whole array of different locations which are laid out across the environment in an amazingly regular triangular grid .	但現在當雷特探索周圍 , 每個細胞都會消失 , 每一個細胞都在一個很棒的區域中 , 一個很棒的規範 。
and if you record from several grid cells shown here in different colors each one has a gridlike firing pattern across the environment , and each cell's gridlike firing pattern is shifted slightly relative to the other cells .	如果你從數個圖片記錄出來 , 每個細胞都有不同的顏色 , 每個細胞都有一堆圖模式 , 每個細胞都稍微相互相相相相相相對 。
so the red one fires on this grid and the green one on this one and the blue on on this one .	所以紅色的紅色之一 , 在這張圖上有綠色的紅色之一 。
so together , it's as if the rat can put a virtual grid of firing locations across its environment a bit like the latitude and longitude lines that you'd find on a map , but using triangles .	所以 , 結合起來就像拉丁文可以把虛擬的地點放在周圍的環境中 , 像是拉丁丁裔和長期的線索 , 但用三角形來看 , 使用三角形 。
and as it moves around , the electrical activity can pass from one of these cells to the next cell to keep track of where it is , so that it can use its own movements to know where it is in its environment .	當它移動到周圍 , 電動活動可以從下一個細胞到下一個細胞 , 讓它可以使用它自己的運動 , 所以它可以用它自己的運動來了解它在環境中 。
do people have grid cells ?	人們有灰質細胞嗎 ?
well because all of the gridlike firing patterns have the same axes of symmetry , the same orientations of grid , shown in orange here , it means that the net activity of all of the grid cells in a particular part of the brain should change according to whether we're running along these six directions or running along one of the six directions in between .	嗯 , 因為所有的圖案都有相同的圖案 , 相同的對稱 , 相同的軌跡 , 它意味著 , 在或橘色細胞中 , 它意味著 , 大腦應該改變大腦的神經元活動 , 或橘色細胞之間的變化 。
so we can put people in an mri scanner and have them do a little video game like the one i showed you and look for this signal .	我們可以把人們放在一個mri掃描儀器裡 , 像我展示給你們看這個訊號 。
and indeed , you do see it in the human entorhinal cortex , which is the same part of the brain that you see grid cells in rats .	事實上 , 你在人類企業皮質皮質上看到它的大腦和雨林一樣 。
so back to homer .	所以回到家鄉 。
he's probably remembering where his car was in terms of the distances and directions to extended buildings and boundaries around the location where he parked .	他可能記得他的車子在哪裡 , 他的車子在哪裡 , 讓他公園的距離 , 在那裡他公園的距離 。
and that would be represented by the firing of boundarydetecting cells .	那會被限制的細胞呈現出來 。
he's also remembering the path he took out of the car park , which would be represented in the firing of grid cells .	他也記得他把車子從車子裡拿出來的路徑 , 這會代表在圖片中呈現出來 。
now both of these kinds of cells can make the place cells fire .	兩種細胞都可以製造細胞消防細胞 。
and he can return to the location where he parked by moving so as to find where it is that best matches the firing pattern of the place cells in his brain currently with the stored pattern where he parked his car .	他無法回顧他公園的位置 , 讓他在大腦中最好的魔法模式 , 找到最好的矩形模式 , 把他的車子放在他的腦袋裡 。
and that guides him back to that location irrespective of visual cues like whether his car's actually there .	這引導他回到那裏的視覺分子 , 比如他的車子是否真的在那裡 。
maybe it's been towed .	也許它已經被嚇壞了 。
but he knows where it was , so he knows to go and get it .	但他知道它在哪裡 , 所以他知道要去哪裡 。
so beyond spatial memory , if we look for this gridlike firing pattern throughout the whole brain , we see it in a whole series of locations which are always active when we do all kinds of autobiographical memory tasks , like remembering the last time you went to a wedding , for example .	所以 , 蜜蜂記憶記憶 , 如果我們尋找這個圖案 , 我們就在整個腦部中看到它的整個大腦中 , 總是活躍於我們做各種自動化的記憶記憶記憶記憶記憶任務 , 比如記住你上一次去 , 比如記住你去的時候 , 比如記住的最後一次 , 舉個例子 。
so it may be that the neural mechanisms for representing the space around us are also used for generating visual imagery so that we can recreate the spatial scene , at least , of the events that have happened to us when we want to imagine them .	所以這可能是我們周遭的神經機制 , 代表我們周圍的空間 , 同時 , 我們可以調整視視覺影像 , 至少 , 當我們想要想像它們的時候 。
so if this was happening , your memories could start by place cells activating each other via these dense interconnections and then reactivating boundary cells to create the spatial structure of the scene around your viewpoint .	所以如果這發生了 , 你的記憶可以從細胞活動中開始 , 讓彼此互聯繫在一起 , 然後反應反應反應反應在你的觀點上 , 創造出脊椎細胞的螢幕結構 。
and grid cells could move this viewpoint through that space .	細胞可以透過這個空間移動這個觀點 。
another kind of cell , head direction cells , which i didn't mention yet , they fire like a compass according to which way you're facing .	另一種細胞 , 頭部細胞 , 我還沒有提到 , 他們像同情心一樣 。
they could define the viewing direction from which you want to generate an image for your visual imagery , so you can imagine what happened when you were at this wedding , for example .	他們可以定義你的視覺圖像的圖像 , 所以你可以想像一下 , 當你在這個圖片時 , 你就可以想像一下發生什麼事 。
so this is just one example of a new era really in cognitive neuroscience where we're beginning to understand psychological processes like how you remember or imagine or even think in terms of the actions of the billions of individual neurons that make up our brains .	這只是在認知神經科學的例子之一 , 我們開始了解心理學過程 , 比如你如何記住心理學過程中的數十億個個人神經元的行為 。
thank you very much .	謝謝大家 。
imagine a global security driven by collaboration among agencies , government , the private sector and the public . that's not just the distant hope of opensource fans , it's the vision of james stavridis , the supreme commander of nato , who shares vivid moments from recent military history to explain why security of the future should be built with bridges rather than walls .	想像一下全球安全局驅動的全球安全驅動機 , 私人部門和公共 。 這不僅僅僅僅是開放的 , 它就是詹姆斯•史蒂夫的願景 , 它就是詹姆斯•史蒂夫 , 他是從軍隊的歷史上分享 , 為何時尚未曾和國際安全的未來 。

james stavridis: how nato's supreme commander thinks about global security	詹姆斯史蒂夫:natototossstrichman思考全球安全性 。
i'm gonna talk a little bit about opensource security , because we've got to get better at security in this 21st century .	我要談一點關於開放的安全 , 因為我們必須更好安全的安全 , 因為我們必須更好安全 。
let me start by saying , let's look back to the 20th century , and kind of get a sense of how that style of security worked for us .	讓我先說 , 咱們回到20世紀的安全感 , 有點了解安全 。
this is verdun , a battlefield in france just north of the nato headquarters in belgium .	這是廣告 , 在法國的北部 , 一個蝙蝠的北極北極 。
at verdun , in 1916 , over a 300day period , 700 , 000 people were killed , so about 2 , 000 a day .	1916年 , 在1916年 , 超過300000000000000人死了 , 所以每天都死了 。
if you roll it forward 20thcentury security into the second world war , you see the battle of stalingrad , 300 days , 2 million people killed .	如果你把它轉向第二次世界大戰 , 你可以看到史塔勒斯坦畢業 , 300天 , 300天 , 2百萬人殺死 。
we go into the cold war , and we continue to try and build walls .	我們進入冷戰戰爭 , 我們繼續嘗試建造牆壁 。
we go from the trench warfare of the first world war to the maginot line of the second world war , and then we go into the cold war , the iron curtain , the berlin wall .	我們從第一個世界大戰的熱情 , 到第二次世界大戰 , 然後我們進入冷戰 , 然後我們進入冷戰時 , 柏林牆壁 。
my thesis for us today is , instead of building walls to create security , we need to build bridges .	我今天的噪音是 , 不是建築牆壁來創造安全 , 我們需要建造橋樑 。
this is a famous bridge in europe .	這是歐洲的橋樑 。
it's the bridge over the drina river , the subject of a novel by ivo andrić , and it talks about how , in that very troubled part of europe and the balkans , over time there's been enormous building of walls .	這是在飲料的橋上 , 橋樑的主題 , 亞里斯的主題 , 談到歐洲和巴爾的主題 , 談到 , 在那裏 , 當時有很大的建築物 。
more recently , in the last decade , we begin to see these communities start , hesitatingly , to come together .	最近十年來 , 在過去十年間 , 我們開始看到這些社區開始 , 把這些社區開始 , 一起合作 。
i would argue , again , opensource security is about connecting the international , the interagency , the privatepublic , and lashing it together with strategic communication , largely in social networks .	我再說一次 , 開放的國家安全是關聯國際網路、私人、私人溝通、私人溝通、私人溝通 , 與策略之間的關係 。
so let me talk a little bit about why we need to do that , because our global commons is under attack in a variety of ways , and none of the sources of threat to the global commons will be solved by building walls .	讓我談談一下為什麼我們需要這麼做 , 因為我們的全球共同共同點 , 因為我們的全球公共攻擊 , 沒有任何威脅到全球共同共同共同點 。
now , i'm a sailor , obviously .	現在 , 我是個sailor , 很顯然 。

two trillion a year .	每年有兩兆美元 。
that's just under the gdp of great britain .	這只是在英國的gdp下 。
so this cyber sea , which we know endlessly is the fundamental piece of radical openness , is very much under threat as well .	所以這個網路海洋 , 我們知道無止止止止止是基本的開放 , 非常低的威脅 。
another thing i worry about in the global commons is the threat posed by trafficking , by the movement of narcotics , opium , here coming out of afghanistan through europe over to the united states .	另一個我擔心全球共同點是威脅的威脅 , 由奈米生物、鴉片、鴉片、鴉片、鴉片、歐洲各地的運動 。

i would argue that we will not deliver security solely from the barrel of a gun .	我會說 , 我們不會把槍枝放在槍枝上 。

eightyfive percent cannot read when they enter the security forces of afghanistan .	當他們進入安全的百分之八十 , 無法讀到阿富汗時 ,

this is a us navy warship .	這是美國奈米戰爭 。

to give you one example of the impact this can have , this little boy , eight years old , walked with his mother two days to come to the eye clinic put on by the comfort .	為了給各位一個例子 , 這個小男孩 , 八歲 , 八歲 , 和他的母親一起走進診所 。
when he was fitted , over his extremely myopic eyes , he suddenly looked up and said , " mama , veo el mundo . "	當他被送到他的眼睛時 , 他突然突然看到 , 他說: 「 馬馬拉 , 老鼠 , 老鼠 , 老鼠 。 」

it shows role models to young men and women about fitness and about life that i would argue help create security for us .	它顯示role模型讓年輕男女和女性有關生活的人生 , 我會爭議幫助我們創造安全 。

yeah , we laugh , but this is how we move the message , and moving that message is how we connect international , interagency , privatepublic , and these social nets to help create security .	是的 , 我們笑 , 但這就是我們如何移動訊息 , 而訊息就是我們如何連結國際、私人、私人、私人、私人、私人、私人、私人、私人、私人、私人、私人的能力 。

you have to dial it in , and as i think about how we create security in this 21st century , there will be times when we will apply hard power in true war and crisis , but there will be many instances , as we've talked about today , where our militaries can be part of creating 21stcentury security , international , interagency , privatepublic , connected with competent communication .	你必須把它放在21世紀內創造安全的安全和危機溝通時 , 我們將會在真正戰爭和危機 , 但有許多時間 , 當我們談到真正戰爭和危機 , 我們的軍隊可以創造21世紀的一部分 , 我們的軍隊可以創造21世紀 , 國際安全、國際安全、國際關係、國際關係、國際關係 。
i would close by saying that we heard earlier today about wikipedia . i use wikipedia all the time to look up facts , and as all of you appreciate , wikipedia is not created by 12 brilliant people locked in a room writing articles .	我今天會說 , 我們聽過維基百科 , 我用維基百科 , 每次你都很欣賞 , 維基百科 , 而你們所有人都在寫作文章中 , 維基百科人都在寫作文章中 。
wikipedia , every day , is tens of thousands of people inputting information , and every day millions of people withdrawing that information .	維基百科 , 每天都有數千人在推特資訊中 , 每天有數百萬人用draw資訊 。
it's a perfect image for the fundamental point that no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	這是一個完美的影像 , 沒有人人在想一起思考的基本圖像 。
no one person , no one alliance , no one nation , no one of us is as smart as all of us thinking together .	沒有人人 , 沒有人任何人 , 都沒有人 , 我們都想在一起 。
the vision statement of wikipedia is very simple: a world in which every human being can freely share in the sum of all knowledge .	維基百科的願景是非常簡單的:一個人可以自由分享在所有知識中分享 。
my thesis for you is that by combining international , interagency , privatepublic , strategic communication , together , in this 21st century , we can create the sum of all security .	我的噪音是 , 國際、私人、私人、私人、私人溝通、策略、策略、策略、在21世紀中 , 我們可以創造出所有安全的成果 。
